Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Four Divisions of Nazm and Ma'na in Hanafi Usul
Author enumerates the fourfold classification of textual types relevant to Shari'a rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any Shari'a text according to the Hanafi fourfold division of nazm and ma'na and identify the specific subcategory within each division.

Core Idea
The Hanafi usul divides texts into four quadrants: word type, clarity, usage mode, and implication—each with four subcategories.

This lesson introduces the foundational taxonomy of textual analysis in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author systematically divides the study of revealed texts (nazm) and meaning (ma'na) into four broad divisions, each further subdivided into four types. Understanding this classification is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Qur'an and Sunnah according to the Hanafi method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall scheme
Recognize that the author presents four main divisions (taqasim) each with four subcategories, totalling sixteen, but the second division also has four opposites, making twenty.
The total is 20: 4 + (4+4) + 4 + 4 = 20.
2
Analyze the first division: wad' (coinage)
The first division categorizes words by how they are coined: khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), mu'awwal (interpreted).
This division focuses on the linguistic structure of the word itself.
3
Analyze the second division: clarity of meaning
The second division ranks texts by clarity: zahir (manifest), nass (explicit), mufassar (clearly explained), muhkam (firm). Their opposites are khafi (hidden), mushkil (difficult), mujmal (ambiguous), mutashabih (unclear).
This division is critical for determining how binding the text is.
4
Analyze the third division: literal and figurative usage
The third division covers modes of expression: haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (clear), kinayah (allusive).
This helps distinguish direct from indirect meanings.
5
Analyze the fourth division: textual implications
The fourth division deals with how the text indicates a ruling: 'ibarat al-nass (direct), isharat al-nass (indirect), dalalat al-nass (inferential), iqtida' al-nass (requirement).
This division is unique to Hanafi usul and expands the scope of derived rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَقْسَامُ النَّظْمِ وَالْمَعْنَى فِيْمَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى مَعْرِفَةِ أَحْكَامِ الشَّرْعِ أَرْبَعَةٌ الْأَوَّلُ فِي وُجُوْهِ النَّظْم صِيْغَةً وَلُغَةً وَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةٌ ترجمہ : - اور نظم اور معنی کی اقسام (تقسیمات ) اس چیز میں جو راجع ہے شریعت کے احکام کی معرفت کی طرف چار ہیں ۔ پہلی تقسیم صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے وضع کے اعتبار سے ) نظم کی قسموں کے بارے میں ہے اور وہ چار قسمیں ہیں ۔ مصنف عالی کتاب اللہ کی تقسیم بیان کر رہے ہیں، یہاں اقسام بمعنی تقسیمات ہیں اور یہ تقسیمات قرآن کے اس حصہ سے متعلق ہے جس کا تعلق احکام شرع کی معرفت سے ہے، ورنہ قرآن کریم تو علوم اور عجائب وغرائب کا منبع ہے، اور یہ چار تقسیمات ہیں جن کے تحت چار چار اقسام ہیں، تو کل سولہ قسمیں ہوئیں مگر دوسری تقسیم میں چار قسموں کے ساتھ ان کے متقابلات بھی چار ہیں اسلئے کل ہیں قسمیں ہو گئیں۔ دلیل حصر یہ ہے کہ کتاب اللہ میں صرف معنی سے بحث ہوگی یا صرف لفظ سے، اگر اول ہے تو تقسیم رابع ہے اور اگر ثانی ہے تو لفظ سے بحث لفظ کے استعمال کے لحاظ سے ہے یا دلالت علی المعنی کے لحاظ سے، اگر اول ہے تو تقسیم ثالث ہے، اور اگر ثانی ہے تو اس میں ظہور وفا کا اعتبار ہوگا یا نہ ہوگا ، اگر اول ہے تو تقسیم ثانی ہے اور اگر ثانی ہے تو تقسیم اول ہے۔ پہلی تقسیم کے تحت چار اقسام ہیں ، خاص ، عام مشترک ، مؤول اور دوسری تقسیم کے تحت چار اقسام ہیں ، ظاہر، نص، مفسر ہمحکم ۔ اور ان کے متقابلات بھی چار ہیں خفی ہمشکل، مجمل ، متشابہ اور تیسری تقسیم کے تحت چار اقسام ہیں حقیقت مجاز ، صریح، کنایہ اور چوتھی تقسیم کے تحت چار اقسام ہیں ،عبارۃ النص ،اشارة النص ، دلالۃ النص، اقتضاء النص ، تو تقسیمات کل چار اور قسمیں کل ہیں ہوئیں۔ پہلی تقسیم نظم کی قسموں کے بارے میں صیغہ اور لغت کے اعتبار سے ہے ،صیغہ کہتے ہیں لفظ کی وہ خاص شکل اور بناوٹ جو اس کو دوسرے صیغوں سے ممتاز کرے جیسے ضرب اور لغت مادہ اور ہیئت کو کہتے ہیں ، مگر یہاں صرف مادہ مراد ہے اس لئے کہ ہیئت کے معنی صیغے نے ادا کر دیے، اور صیغةً ولغہ سے کنایہ وضع مراد ہے، کیونکہ لفظ کی جب وضع ہوتی ہے تو اس میں صیغہ ولغت دونوں ہوتے ہیں تو گویا مصنف یوں کہہ رہے ہیں کہ پہلی تقسیم نظم کی وضع کے اعتبار سے ہے اور اسکی چار قسمیں ہیں خاص، عام مشترک ، مؤول ، آگے سب کی تعریف کریں گے۔
And the divisions of nazm and ma'na in that which relates to knowledge of the rulings of Shari'a are four. The first: concerning the aspects of nazm with respect to sighah and lughah, and it is four. Translation: The divisions of nazm and ma'na in what relates to knowledge of Shari'a rulings are four. The first division concerns the types of nazm from the perspective of sighah and lughah (i.e., wad'), and it has four types. The noble author is describing the division of the Book of Allah. Here 'aqsam' means divisions, and these divisions pertain to that part of the Qur'an which relates to knowledge of Shari'a rulings, otherwise the Qur'an is a source of sciences and wonders. These are four divisions, each having four types, so total sixteen types. However, in the second division, alongside the four types, there are also four opposites, so total twenty types. The proof of the count is that in the Book of Allah, either meaning alone is discussed or word alone. If the first, then the division is the fourth; if the second, then discussion of the word is either in terms of usage or in terms of indication of meaning. If the first, then the division is the third; if the second, then consideration of clarity or not occurs. If the first, then the division is the second; if the second, then the division is the first. Under the first division are four types: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. Under the second division are four types: zahir, nass, mufassar, muhkam. And their opposites are also four: khafi, mushkil, mujmal, mutashabih. Under the third division are four types: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah. Under the fourth division are four types: 'ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, iqtida' al-nass. Thus the divisions total four and the types total twenty. The first division concerns types of nazm with respect to sighah and lughah. Sighah is the specific form and structure of a word that distinguishes it from other sighahs, like daraba. Lughah is the root and form, but here only the root is intended because the meaning of form is already given by sighah. And by 'sighatan wa lughatan', wad' (convention) is meant, because when a word is coined, both sighah and lughah are present. So the author says that the first division is from the perspective of wad' of nazm, and it has four types: khas, 'amm, mushtarak, mu'awwal. All their definitions will follow.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents the methodological framework for classifying texts in the Qur'an and Sunnah for the purpose of deriving legal rulings. The author divides the study into four main divisions (taqasim), each containing four subcategories, making a total of sixteen (with opposites in the second division making twenty). The first division deals with types of wording from the perspective of linguistic coinage (wad'): khas (specific), 'amm (general), mushtarak (homonym), and mu'awwal (interpreted). The second division concerns clarity of meaning: zahir (manifest), nass (explicit), mufassar (clearly explained), muhkam (firm), and their opposites khafi (hidden), mushkil (difficult), mujmal (ambiguous), mutashabih (unclear). The third division deals with literal and figurative usage: haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (clear), kinayah (allusive). The fourth division deals with implications of the text: 'ibarat al-nass (direct indication), isharat al-nass (indirect indication), dalalat al-nass (inferential indication), and iqtida' al-nass (requirement of the text). This classification is essential for hanafi usul al-fiqh to properly understand how each type of text conveys legal rulings. The author explains that these divisions apply to the portion of the Qur'an related to legal rulings, not the theological or other aspects.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word coined for a single known meaning individually.
عام ('amm): A word that encompasses all individuals of its category either in wording or meaning.
ظاہر (zahir): A word with a clear meaning that is probable but not decisive.
نص (nass): A word with a clear meaning that is decisive and not open to ta'wil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many total types are there in the four divisions according to the text?
A) 16
B) 20
C) 24
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of texts into four divisions (wad', clarity, usage, implication) with twenty subtypes provides a systematic framework for precise legal derivation.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
beginner
6 min
Definitions of Khass and 'Amm in Hanafi Usul
Definition of Khass and 'Amm with conditions and exclusions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining conditions of khass and 'amm in Hanafi usul and explain why mushtarak is excluded from khass.

Core Idea
Khass excludes homonyms by requiring individual exclusivity; 'amm includes all members of a category unless specified.

In Hanafi usul, precise definitions of terms like 'khass' and 'amm' are the building blocks of legal interpretation. This lesson unpacks the author's careful wording, showing how each restriction serves to exclude other word types. You will learn to parse these definitions and apply them to understand the scope of texts.

Guided Path
1
Extract the core definitions
Read the Arabic definitions of khass and 'amm. Note that both begin with 'kullu lafz' or 'kullu ism' followed by conditions. Khass is 'a word coined for a known meaning individually'; 'amm is 'a word that encompasses a group of named entities by wording or meaning'.
The definitions are tightly constructed; pay attention to every qualifier.
2
Analyze the restrictions for khass
The definition includes three key restrictions: 'wudi'a' (coined), 'ma'lum' (known), and 'ala al-infiraad' (individually). For each, identify which word type is excluded: 'wudi'a' excludes muhmal (meaningless sounds); 'ma'lum' (if interpreted as known intent) excludes mushtarak (homonym); but the text shows that 'ala al-infiraad definitively excludes mushtarak because khass must be exclusive to one meaning.
Understand that 'ma'lum' can have two interpretations; the text resolves the ambiguity via the individuality condition.
3
Understand the exclusion of mushtarak
The text explains that if 'ma'lum' means 'known intent', then mushtarak is excluded because its intent is not fixed. If 'ma'lum' means 'clearly known', then mushtarak is not excluded because its meanings are clear. However, 'ala al-infiraad excludes mushtarak in both cases because khass must designate a single meaning individually, not shared.
This shows the layered defense in Hanafi usul definitions.
4
Understand the definition of 'amm
'Amm is a word that encompasses all individuals of its category. Encompassment can be by wording (e.g., plural forms like 'al-rijal') or by meaning (e.g., generic sense). The effect is that all members are included unless evidence of specification (takhsis) exists.
Note that 'amm is not absolute; it can be restricted by a khass evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخَاضُ وَهُوَ كُلُّ لَفظ وُضِعَ لِمَعنِّى مَعْلُومٍ عَلَى الانْفِرَادِ وَكُلُّ اِسمٍ وُضِعَ لِمُسَمًّى مَعْلُومٍ عَلَى الانْفِرَادِ وَالعَامُ وَهُوَ كُلَّ لَفْظِ يَنتَظِمُ جَمِعاً مِنَ المُسَمَّيَاتِ لفظاً أَو مَعنى ترجمہ : - خاص اور وہ ہر ایسا لفظ ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معنی معلوم کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر اور ہر ایسا اسم ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معلوم ذات کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر اور عام ہر وہ لفظ ہے جو شامل ہو تمام مسمیات کو لفظاً یا معنی ۔ تشریح:- مصنف ہے خاص و عام کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں ، خاص ہر وہ لفظ ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معلوم معنی کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر، اور ہر وہ اسم ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو ایک معلوم ذات کے لئے۔ وضع کی قید سے مہمل نکل گیا اور معلوم سے مراد اگر معلوم المراد ہے تو اس سے مشترک نکل گیا، اس لئے کہ مشترک معلوم المراد نہیں ہوتا ہے، اور اگر معلوم سے مراد معلوم البیان ہے تو مشترک اس سے نہیں نکلے گا ، اس لئے کہ مشترک کے معنی واضح ہوتے ہیں، پھر مشترک علی الانفراد کی قید سے نکلے گا، کیونکہ علی الانفراد کا مطلب ہے کہ خاص جس معنی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے وہ معنی دوسرے معنی سے بھی منفرد ہو اور افراد سے بھی منفرد ہو، پس خاص کے معنی چونکہ دوسرے معنی سے بھی منفرد ہوتے ہیں یعنی خاص ایک ہی معنی کو شامل ہوتا ہے، تو اس سے مشترک نکل جائے۔
Al-khass: it is every word coined for a known meaning on the basis of individuality, and every noun coined for a known named entity on the basis of individuality. Al-'amm: it is every word that encompasses a group of named entities (musammayat) whether by wording or meaning. Translation: Khass is every word that has been coined for a known meaning in the manner of individuality, and every noun that has been coined for a known entity in the manner of individuality. And 'amm is every word that includes all the musammayat, either in wording or meaning. Explanation: The author is defining khass and 'amm. Khass is every word coined for a known meaning individually, and every noun coined for a known entity. The restriction 'coined' excludes meaningless words (muhmal). 'Known' if it means known intent (ma'lum al-murad) then it excludes mushtarak (homonym) because mushtarak has no fixed intent. If 'known' means clearly known (ma'lum al-bayan) then mushtarak is not excluded because mushtarak's meanings are clear. Then mushtarak is excluded by the restriction 'ala al-infiraad (on individuality) because 'ala al-infiraad means that the meaning for which khass is coined is separate from other meanings and also separate from individuals. Therefore, since the meaning of khass is separate from other meanings, i.e., it covers only one meaning, this excludes mushtarak.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage provides the technical definitions of 'khass' and 'amm' in Hanafi usul. 'Khass' is a word that is coined (by language convention) for a single, known meaning, and it applies to that meaning exclusively in a one-to-one relationship. The definition includes both verbs (or words) and nouns (names of entities). The author carefully uses restrictions to exclude other categories: 'wudi'a' (coined) excludes meaningless sounds (muhmal); 'ma'lum' (known) — if interpreted as 'known intent' excludes homonyms (mushtarak) because homonyms have multiple possible intents; if interpreted as 'clearly known' then homonyms are not excluded because their meanings are clear. However, the second restriction 'ala al-infiraad' (individuation) further excludes homonyms, because a khass word is designated for a single meaning individually, not sharing between meanings. Al-'Amm is defined as a word that encompasses all individuals of its category, whether by wording (e.g., 'al-rijal' for all men) or by meaning (e.g., the generic sense). These definitions are foundational for understanding how general and specific texts operate in deriving legal rulings.

Key Terms
خاص (khass): A word coined for a single known meaning individually.
عام ('amm): A word that encompasses all members of its category (musammayat) either in wording or meaning.
علی الانفراد ('ala al-infiraad): On the basis of individuality, meaning the word applies to one specific meaning only, not shared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What type of word is excluded from the definition of khass by the condition 'ala al-infiraad'?
A) Muhmal (meaningless)
B) Mushtarak (homonym)
C) Mu'awwal (interpreted)
D) Haqiqah (literal)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, khass and 'amm are defined with precise conditions that determine how texts are interpreted in legal reasoning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
6 min
Definitions of Khas and Aam in Hanafi Usul
Defines khas and aam with their classifications and subtypes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khas and aam, identify their subtypes, and apply the definitions to classify words correctly.

Core Idea
Khas indicates a single known entity; aam indicates multiplicity of named entities by wording or meaning.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the precise definitions of 'khas' (specific) and 'aam' (general) are foundational for understanding how legal rulings are derived from textual sources. This passage from Al-Husami provides the classical definitions and subtypes, essential for any usul student to avoid misclassification of terms.

Guided Path
1
Parse the definition of khas
Identify the two definitional components: a word placed for a known meaning individually, and a name for a known entity individually. Note the conditions 'placed' (وضع) excludes meaningless words (muhmal), 'known' excludes ambiguous homonyms (mushtarak), and 'individual manner' (على الانفراد) excludes aam.
The condition 'individual manner' ensures exclusivity to one meaning.
2
Identify the three subtypes of khas
Recognize khas jins (specific genus, e.g., 'insan' – human), khas naw' (specific type, e.g., 'rajul' – man), and khas 'ayn (specific individual, e.g., 'Khalid'). The author provides two definitions to emphasize the exclusivity of khas 'ayn.
Khas 'ayn has no share in any other entity.
3
Understand the definition of aam
Aam is every word that encompasses a group of named entities, either by wording (e.g., plural forms) or by meaning (e.g., 'man' in the sense of generality). Its multiplicity is inherent, not accidental.
Multiplicity can be literal (صيغ الجموع) or meaning-based (أدوات العموم).
4
Apply the definitions to classify words
Using the conditions, classify given Arabic terms as khas (with subtype) or aam. For example, 'Rashid' is khas 'ayn; 'qawm' is aam; 'hayawan' is khas jins.
If a word appears in a general context but is singular, it may still be khas; aam requires explicit indication of multiplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخَاضُ وَهُوَ كُلُّ لَفظ وُضِعَ لِمَعنِّى مَعْلُومٍ عَلَى الانْفِرَادِ وَكُلُّ اِسمٍ وُضِعَ لِمُسَمًّى مَعْلُومٍ عَلَى الانْفِرَادِ وَالعَامُ وَهُوَ كُلَّ لَفْظِ يَنتَظِمُ جَمِعاً مِنَ المُسَمَّيَاتِ لفظاً أَو مَعنى ترجمہ : - خاص اور وہ ہر ایسا لفظ ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معنی معلوم کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر اور ہر ایسا اسم ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معلوم ذات کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر اور عام ہر وہ لفظ ہے جو شامل ہو تمام مسمیات کو لفظاً یا معنی ۔ تشریح:- مصنف ہے خاص و عام کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں ، خاص ہر وہ لفظ ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو معلوم معنی کے لئے انفراد کے طریقہ پر، اور ہر وہ اسم ہے جو وضع کیا گیا ہو ایک معلوم ذات کے لئے۔ وضع کی قید سے مہمل نکل گیا اور معلوم سے مراد اگر معلوم المراد ہے تو اس سے مشترک نکل گیا، اس لئے کہ مشترک معلوم المراد نہیں ہوتا ہے، اور اگر معلوم سے مراد معلوم البیان ہے تو مشترک اس سے نہیں نکلے گا ، اس لئے کہ مشترک کے معنی واضح ہوتے ہیں، پھر مشترک علی الانفراد کی قید سے نکلے گا، کیونکہ علی الانفراد کا مطلب ہے کہ خاص جس معنی کے لئے وضع کیا گیا ہے وہ معنی دوسرے معنی سے بھی منفرد ہو اور افراد سے بھی منفرد ہو، پس خاص کے معنی چونکہ دوسرے معنی سے بھی منفرد ہوتے ہیں یعنی خاص ایک ہی معنی کو شامل ہوتا ہے، تو اس سے مشترک نکل جائے گا، کیونکہ مشترک دوسرے معنی سے منفرد نہیں ہوتا ہے، بلکہ ایک سے زیادہ معنی کو شامل ہوتا ہے ۔ اور خاص کے معنی چونکہ افراد سے بھی منفرد ہوتے ہیں یعنی بہت سے افراد کو شامل نہیں ہوتے تو اس سے عام نکل جائے گا کیونکہ عام کے معنی افراد سے منفرد نہیں ہوتے بلکہ بہت سے افراد کو شامل ہوتے ہیں۔ یہاں ایک بات ذہن میں رکھیں کہ خاص کے لفظ سے جو خصوص مفہوم ہو رہا ہے وہ تین طرح کا ہے۔ (۱) خصوص جنس یعنی معنی کے اعتبار سے اس کی جنس خاص ہو ، اگر چہ اس کا مصداق متعدد ہو جیسے انسان، ا حیوان (۲) خصوص نوع یعنی معنی کے اعتبار سے اس کی نوع خاص ہو ، اگر چہ اس کا مصداق متعدد ہو جیسے رجل امرأة (۳) خصوص عين یعنی شخص معین ہو جیسے راشد ، خالد وغیرہ۔ مصنف نے یہاں خاص کی دو تعریفیں کی ہیں، اگر چہ پہلی تعریف خاص کی تینوں قسموں کو شامل تھی ،مگر خاص کی تیسری قسم خاص العین کے لئے مستقل الگ سے تعریف کی، جو صرف اسی کو شامل ہو، پہلی دو قسموں کو شامل نہ ہو، کیونکہ خاص العین خصوصیت میں ایسا کامل ہے کہ اس میں کسی طرح کی کوئی شرکت نہیں ہے۔ عام کہتے ہیں جو بہت سارے افراد کو شامل ہو لفظاً یا معنی ، یعنی عام کے معنی موضوع لہ میں تعدد ہوتا ہے، اس لئے وہ براہ راست افراد پر دلالت کرتا ہے، پھر تعدد دو طرح کا ہے، لفظی تعدد جیسے جمع کے تمام صیغے اور معنی تعدد جیسے من، ما، قوم ، ربط وغیرہ۔ بہر حال خاص میں تو حد و انفراد لوظ ہوتا ہے اور عام میں تعدد ہوتا ہے، اگر خاص میں کہیں تعد د نظر آئے گا تو وہ معنی موضوع لہ کے افراد و جزئیات کی وجہ سے ہوگا انتہی
The specific: it is every word placed for a known meaning in a singular manner, and every name placed for a known named entity in a singular manner. And the general: it is every word that encompasses a group of named entities, by wording or meaning. Translation: Khas is every word placed for a known meaning individually, and every name placed for a known essence individually. And aam is every word that includes all named entities literally or meaning-wise. Commentary: The author is defining khas and aam. Khas is every word placed for a known meaning individually, and every name placed for a known essence individually. The condition 'placed' excludes meaningless words. 'Known' if intended as known reference excludes mushtarak, because mushtarak is not known in reference. But if 'known' means known in clarification, then mushtarak is not excluded because its meanings are clear. Then the condition 'individual manner' excludes mushtarak because khas is exclusive to one meaning, while mushtarak includes multiple meanings. Also it excludes aam because khas does not encompass many individuals, while aam does. Note: The specific meaning from the word khas is of three types: (1) specificity of genus (e.g., insan, hayawan), (2) specificity of type (e.g., rajul, imra'ah), (3) specificity of individual (e.g., Rashid, Khalid). The author gave two definitions of khas: the first includes all three types, but the second is specifically for 'ain, which is exclusive to that one. Aam is what includes many individuals by wording or meaning; its meaning involves multiplicity, and it indicates individuals directly. Multiplicity is of two types: literal (e.g., plural forms) and meaning-based (e.g., man, ma, qawm, etc.). In short, khas is limited and individual, while aam has multiplicity. If multiplicity appears in khas, it is due to the individuals and particulars of the intended meaning. End.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a definition section explaining the terms khas (specific) and aam (general) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author defines khas as a word placed for a single known meaning in a singular manner, or a name for a specific known entity. This definition excludes meaningless words (muhmal) through the condition 'placed'. It also excludes mushtarak (homonym) through 'known' and 'individual manner' because mushtarak has multiple meanings. Similarly, it excludes aam because khas does not refer to multiple individuals. The author then explains three subtypes of khas: specificity of genus (e.g., 'human' includes many individuals but is specific as a genus), specificity of type (e.g., 'man' is more specific than 'human'), and specificity of individual (e.g., a proper name like 'Rashid'). The second definition of khaas is specifically for the 'individual' type to emphasize its uniqueness. Aam is defined as a word that includes many individuals, either by literal form (like plurals) or by meaning (like 'whoever', 'whatever', 'people', etc.). The key point is that khaas is limited to one meaning or one set, while aam inherently indicates multiplicity.

Key Terms
خاص (khaas): A word placed for a single known meaning individually, or a name for a single known entity individually
عام (aam): A word that encompasses a group of named entities, either by wording or meaning

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 'Man' (rajul)
C) 'Rashid' (a proper name)
D) 'Whoever' (man)

Key Takeaway
Khas indicates a specific meaning or entity individually; aam indicates multiplicity by wording or meaning.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Ruling on General Words (Aam): Definitive in Scope
States the Hanafi ruling on aam's definitive nature and the ikhtilaf with al-Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the definitive nature of aam and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concept of takhsis.

Core Idea
Aam is qat'i until a particularizer is found — the default is certainty, not speculation.

This passage presents a foundational usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. At issue is whether a general word (aam) in the Quran or Sunnah gives a definitive ruling for all its instances or is merely speculative. The Hanafi school holds that aam is qat'i (definitive) by default, while the Shafi'i school considers it zanni (speculative). Understanding this difference is crucial for deriving rulings from revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the claim: aam obligates the ruling on all its individuals 'qat'an wa yaqinan' (absolutely and certainly), just like khas does.
This is the madhhab 'indana (our school) as per the text.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
The text says 'khilafan lil-Shafi'i' — Imam al-Shafi'i holds that aam is zanni, not qat'i.
Shafi'is argue that many general texts have exceptions, so certainty is not possible.
3
Examine the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the mere possibility of takhsis does not negate the definitive nature of aam before a particularizer is discovered.
The text does not elaborate the response, but the dispute is clear.
4
Understand the exception clause
The passage adds an exception: when a known or unknown makhsus attaches (like the riba verse), the general ruling still obligates but with the possibility that the particularization becomes clear through ta'lil (explanation) or tafsir (interpretation).
This shows Hanafis do accept takhsis, but it does not change the default qat'i status.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi jurists apply general texts to all instances unless a contradiction is found; Shafi'is will seek evidence that a particular instance is included, as the default is speculation.
This affects how one approaches a general verse like 'Allah permitted trade'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَحُكْمُهُ أنّه يُوجب الْحُكْمَ فِيْمَا تَنَاوَلَهُ قَطَّعَا ويَقِينًا كَالْخَاصَ فِيْمَا تَنَاوَلَهُ وَهُوَ الْمَذْهَبْ عِنْدَنَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافَعِي إِلَّا أَنَّهُ إِذَا لَحِقَهُ خُصُوصٌ مَعْلُوْمْ أَوْ مَجْهُولٌ كَآيَةِ الزِبُوا فِي الْبَيْعِ فَحِينَئِذٍ يُوجِبُ الحُكْمَ عَلى تَجَوُّزِ أَنَّهُ يَظْهَرُ الْخُصُوصُ فَيْهِ بِتَعْلِيْلِهِ أَوْ بِتَفْسِيْرِهِ ترجمہ : - اور عام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ واجب کرتا ہے حکم کو ان تمام افراد میں جن کو وہ شامل ہوتا ہے قطعی اور یقینی طور پر، جیسا کہ خاص ان تمام افراد میں جن کو وہ شامل ہوتا ہے، اور یہی مذہب ہے ہمارے نزدیک، امام شافعی اللہ کے خلاف ،مگر جب کہ عام کو لاحق ہو جائے مخصص معلوم یا مخصص مجہول جیسا کہ آیت ربو ہے بیج میں ، پس اس وقت عام حکم کو واجب کر یگا اس بات کے احتمال کے ساتھ کہ تخصیص ظاہر ہو جائے عام میں مخصص معلوم کی علت بیان کرنے کی وجہ سے یا مخصص مجہول کی تفسیر کرنے کی وجہ سے۔
And its ruling is that it necessitates the ruling in whatever it encompasses absolutely and certainly, like the specific in what it encompasses. And this is the madhhab according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Except that when it is affected by a known particularizer or an unknown particularizer, like the verse of riba in sale, then it necessitates the ruling with the possibility that the particularization appears in it through its explanation or its interpretation. Translation: The ruling of aam is that it makes the ruling obligatory on all individuals it includes, absolutely and certainly, like khas does in what it includes. This is our school, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. However, when a known or unknown makhsus (particularizer) attaches to it, like the verse of riba in sale, then it necessitates the ruling with the probability that the particularization appears in it by explaining its cause or its interpretation.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal status of general words (aam). According to the Hanafis, a general word (like 'every' or 'all') gives a definitive ruling on all individuals it encompasses, just as a specific word (khas) does. This means that when the Quran or Hadith uses a general expression, the ruling applies to every instance without exception, unless there is a known or unknown particularizer (makhsus) that limits it. The example given is the verse about riba (interest) in sale, which is general but has a particularizer. In such cases, the general ruling is still definitive in principle, but with the possibility that the particularization may become clear through explanation (ta'lil) or interpretation (tafsir). The Shafi'i school differs, considering aam as zanni (speculative) unless there is evidence to support its generality. The key takeaway: Hanafis hold that aam is qat'i by default, while Shafi'is hold it is zanni.

Key Terms
عام (aam): A general word that encompasses multiple individuals; its ruling is definitive (qat'i) until particularization.
مخصص (mukhassis): A particularizer that limits the scope of a general word; can be known (connected or separate) or unknown.
قاطع (qat'i): Definitive, certain; a ruling or text that admits no possibility of alternative interpretation until overridden.
ظني (zanni): Speculative, probable; a ruling or text that is open to alternative interpretations and not certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how does a general word (aam) apply to its individuals before any particularizer is found?
A) It applies speculatively, subject to possible exceptions.
B) It applies definitively and certainly to all individuals.
C) It does not apply until a particularizer is identified.
D) It applies only if the text is from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general word (aam) is definitively binding on all its instances until a particularizer is proven.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling of 'Amm: Hanafi Position of Certainty
Statements the Hanafi ruling on 'Amm's definitiveness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Amm as qat'i, explain the exception of takhsis, and identify the practical consequence of the Hanafi vs Shafi'i position on 'Amm.

Core Idea
'Amm is definitive in its application until a specific exception is proven; after takhsis it becomes probable but still binding.

This passage clarifies a foundational Hanafi usul principle: general words in the Quran and Sunnah ('Amm) are legally certain (qat'i) and apply to all individuals they cover, just like specific terms (Khass). This differs from Imam al-Shafi'i's view that 'Amm is only probable (zanni). The author then explains that when a specificr (mukhassis) is attached, the general term loses its certainty and becomes probable, allowing the possibility of further exceptions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct istinbat (derivation) of fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim about 'Amm
State that the Hanafi school holds 'Amm to be qat'i (definitive) in applying the ruling to all individuals it covers, just like Khass.
This is the maddhab 'indana (our school).
2
Recognize the exception: takhsis changes the status
When a known or unknown mukhassis (specificr) attaches to 'Amm, it loses its definitiveness and becomes zanni (probable).
Example: the verse about killing polytheists was specified by the verse granting asylum.
3
Distinguish known and unknown mukhassis
Known mukhassis (makhsus ma'lum) has a clear cause (ta'lil); unknown mukhassis (makhsus majhul) requires explanation (tafsir). Both reduce 'Amm to probability.
In both cases, the remaining individuals of 'Amm are applied with zann.
4
Apply the rule to the examples given
Work through the examples: 'kill the polytheists' (known mukhassis) and 'trade vs riba' (unknown? actually riba is an exception).
Note how the mukhassis is identified and how it affects the 'Amm.
5
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
For Shafi'i, 'Amm is always zanni, so they apply it with caution from the outset. For Hanafi, it is qat'i until takhsis, after which it becomes zanni.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi applies 'Amm broadly until an exception is proven; Shafi'i requires more evidence to confirm applicability.

الفيضُ الحجازي
۱۹
شرح اردو المنحها الى امى
تشریح : ۔ مصنف ہے خاص و عام کی تعریف کے بعد اب حکم بیان کر رہے ہیں مگر صرف عام کا حکم بیان کیا ہے اور خاص کے حکم کی طرف صرف اشارہ کر دیا کالخاص فيما تناوله، کہہ کر، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے خاص کا حکم جمہور کے نزدیک غیر مختلف فیہ ہے اس لئے صرف اشارہ کر دیا، اور عام کا حکم مختلف فیہ ہے اس لئے اس کو تفصیل سے بیان کیا ۔ بہر حال خاص کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے مدلول پر قطعی اور یقینی طور پر اس طرح شامل ہوتا ہے کہ اس میں غیر کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا، جیسے ثلثة قروءمیں ثلثہ خاص ہے، یہ اپنے مدلول کو قطعی طور پر شامل ہے،ثلثہ کا اطلاق نہ تین سے کم پر ہوتا نہ تین سے زیادہ پر۔
الله.
اور عام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے تمام افراد میں قطعی اور یقینی طور پر حکم کو واجب کرتا ہے ،جس طرح خاص قطعی ہوتا ہے، احناف کا مسلک یہی ہے، بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ عام میں توقف کیا جائے گا جب تک کوئی دلیل معین قائم نہ ہو جائے ، یوجب الحکم کہہ کر مصنف نے اس کی تردید کی بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں عام اگر واحد کا صیغہ ہے تو ایک پر دلالت کرے گا اور جمع کا صیغہ ہے تو تین پر دلالت کرے گا اور باقی افراد میں توقف ہو گا دلیل قائم ہونے تک، فيما تناولہ سے مصنف نے اس کی تردید کردی ، امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک عام قطعی نہیں بلکہ ظنی ہے ، تو مصنف ان نے قطعاً ويقينا سے اس قول کی تردید کردی۔ الااذا لحقه :- سے مصنف یہ بتارہے ہیں کہ عام قطعی ہوتا ہے مگر کسی دلیل مخصص سے عام کے اندر اگر تخصیص ہو جائے تو پھر عام قطعی نہیں رہتا ہے، بلکہ ظنی ہو جاتا ہے، اس وقت وہ صرف حکم کو واجب کرتا ہے مگر اس احتمال کے ساتھ کہ جس دلیل سے پہلے کچھ افراد عام میں سے خاص کئے گئے ہیں ، ہوسکتا ہے کہ اس دلیل کے تحت عام کے کچھ اور افراد بھی آجائیں ، اور وہ بھی عام کے حکم سے خارج ہو جائیں جیسے اللہ تعالٰی کا ارشاد فا قتلوا المشركين مشرکین کو قتل کر وہ مشرکین عام ہے ، تمام مشرکین سے قتال کا حکم ہے، مگر وان احد من المشركين استجارك فاجرہ مشرکین میں سے کوئی پناہ مانگے تو پناہ دے دو، اس کے ذریعہ تخصیص ہو گئی یعنی امن طلب کرنے والے مشرکین سے خارج ہو گئے ، ان سے قتال نہیں کیا جائے گا اور نصوص میں اصل علت ہے ہم نے اس کی علت نکالی لڑائی سے عاجز ہونا‘ لہذا اس علت کی وجہ سے مشرکین میں سے عورتیں، بوڑھے، اپا نچ ، اندھے اور راہسبین سب کی تخصیص ہو گئی یعنی ان سے بھی قتال نہ ہوگا مخصص معلوم کی مثال ہے۔
الحاصل جب عام میں حصص معلوم یا مجہول کے ذریعے تخصیص ہو جائے گی تو عام اپنے باقی افراد میں عمل کو واجب کرے گا ظنیت کے ساتھ ۔ جیسے اللہ تعالی کا ارشاد احل الله البيع وحرم الربو میں بیچ لام استغراق داخل
ہونے کی وجہ سے عام ہے، جو تمام بیوع کوحتی کہ ربو کو بھی شامل ہے، پھر حرم الربو کہہ کر بیع ربو کی تخصیص کی گئی یعنی
And its ruling is that it necessitates the ruling in all that it includes definitively and certainly, like the specific in all that it includes. This is the madhhab with us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, except that when it is affected by a known or unknown specificr, like the verse of usury in sale, then it necessitates the ruling with the probability that the specification appears in it by its cause or by its explanation. Translation: And the ruling of 'amm is that it obligates the ruling in all individuals that it includes, definitively and certainly, just as the specific obligates the ruling in all individuals that it includes. And this is the madhhab with us, contrary to Imam Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. But when 'amm is affected by a known or unknown specificr, like the verse of usury in sale, then at that time it will obligate the ruling with the probability that specification appears in 'amm, due to stating the cause (ta'lil) of the known specificr or due to the explanation (tafsir) of the unknown specificr. Commentary: The author (mussannif), after defining specific and general, now states the ruling but only mentions the ruling of 'amm and merely hints at the ruling of specific by saying 'like the specific in what it includes'. The reason is that the ruling of specific is undisputed among the majority, so he just hinted, while the ruling of 'amm is disputed, so he explained it in detail. In any case, the ruling of specific is that it includes its denotation definitively and certainly such that there is no probability of other, like 'thalatha' (three) in 'thalathatu quru' (three periods) is specific, it definitely includes its denotation; the application of 'thalatha' is neither less than three nor more than three. And the ruling of 'amm is that it obligates the ruling in all its individuals definitively and certainly, just as specific is definitive. This is the Hanafi madhhab. Some people say that 'amm is suspended (tawaqquf) until a specific evidence is established; the author refuted them by saying 'yujibu al-hukm' (it obligates the ruling). Some people say that if 'amm is in the form of singular, it indicates one, and if plural, it indicates three, and the remaining individuals are suspended until evidence; the author refuted them by 'fima tana'walahu' (in what it includes). Imam Shafi'i holds that 'amm is not definitive but probable; so the author refuted that with 'qat'an wa yaqinan' (definitively and certainly). 'Illa idha lahiqahu...' the author shows that 'amm is definitive, but when a specificr (mukhassis) is attached, then 'amm is no longer definitive but becomes probable. At that time it only obligates the ruling with the probability that further individuals may be excluded, like Allah's saying 'faqtulu al-mushrikeen' (kill the polytheists) – 'mushrikeen' is 'amm, commanding fighting all polytheists, but 'wa in ahadun min al-mushrikeen istajaraka fa-ajirhu' (if one of the polytheists seeks asylum, grant him asylum) specifies, i.e., those seeking protection are excluded from fighting. And in the texts, the original cause is extracted: inability to fight; therefore by this cause, among the polytheists, women, old, disabled, blind, and monks are all specified, i.e., fighting them is not allowed. This is an example of a known specificr. Conclusion: when 'amm is specified by a known or unknown specificr, it obligates action on the remaining individuals with probability. Like Allah's saying 'ahalla Allah al-bay' wa harrama al-riba' – 'al-bay' is 'amm due to the lam istighraq (the lām of inclusiveness), including all sales, even riba, then 'harrama al-riba' specified the sale of riba.
Source pages p. 19

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on 'Amm (general terms) and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position. The author first states the Hanafi rule: 'Amm is decisive (qat'i) in applying the ruling to all individuals it covers, exactly like Khass (specific terms). This is the established Hanafi madhhab, contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i who holds 'Amm is probable (zanni). The author refutes other views, such as those who suspend judgment (tawaqquf) until evidence, or who limit 'Amm to literal minimums (singular=one, plural=three). He then explains the exception: when a specificr (mukhassis), known or unknown, attaches to 'Amm, it loses its decisiveness and becomes probable, because further individuals might be excluded. He provides the example of the verse 'kill the polytheists' which is general, but is specified by the verse granting asylum and by the derived cause of inability to fight, excluding women, elderly, etc. Another example is 'Allah has permitted trade and forbidden riba' – 'trade' is general, but riba is excepted. The practical outcome is that in Hanafi usul, 'Amm is applied with certainty until a valid specificr is found; after specification, the remaining individuals are applied with probability.

Key Terms
عام ('Amm): لفظ جو متعدد افراد پر دلالت کرے
قطعی (Qat'i): یقینی، جس میں احتمال نہ ہو
ظنی (Zanni): احتمالی، جس میں دوسرا احتمال ہو
تخصیص (Takhsis): عام میں سے بعض افراد کو خارج کرنا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does 'Amm become zanni?
A) Always
B) Before takhsis
C) After takhsis by a known or unknown specificr
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that 'Amm is qat'i before takhsis and zanni after it is central to correct istinbat, ensuring both certainty and flexibility in deriving fiqh rulings.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Ruling on Amm: Qat'i Before Takhsis, Zanni After
Explains Hanafi position that amm is qati before and zanni after takhsis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that amm is qat'i before takhsis and zanni after, apply this principle to a Quranic example, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a general term is definitive until specified; after specification, it remains binding but conjectural.

This lesson delves into a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the definitive nature of general terms (amm) and how specification (takhsis) affects their evidentiary value. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct istinbat (derivation) of rulings from scripture. The passage contrasts the Hanafi view with that of Imam al-Shafi'i and others, using Quranic verses to illustrate the transformation from qat'i to zanni after takhsis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi claim about amm before takhsis
The text states that amm is qat'i (definitive) in indicating its ruling on all individuals. Note the phrase 'qat'an wa yaqinan' which emphasizes certainty.
This is the core of the Hanafi position.
2
Locate the dispute with other schools
The text mentions that some (including Shafi'is) hold that amm requires pause until evidence, meaning it is inherently zanni. Identify the opposing views and their basis.
The author refutes these by asserting the definitive nature of amm.
3
Trace the effect of takhsis on amm
The text explains that after specification, amm becomes zanni (conjectural) for the remaining individuals. Understand why: because the mukhassis may itself be subject to qiyas, leading to further specification.
This is unique to Hanafis; others may hold that takhsis shows amm was never qat'i.
4
Apply to a Quranic example
Work through the verse 'kill the polytheists' and its specification. Show how the general command is specified by the exception, then further by qiyas, thus the ruling on remaining polytheists is zanni.
This demonstrates the practical consequence of the Hanafi principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف ہے خاص و عام کی تعریف کے بعد اب حکم بیان کر رہے ہیں مگر صرف عام کا حکم بیان کیا ہے اور خاص کے حکم کی طرف صرف اشارہ کر دیا کالخاص فيما تناوله، کہہ کر، اس کی وجہ یہ ہے خاص کا حکم جمہور کے نزدیک غیر مختلف فیہ ہے اس لئے صرف اشارہ کر دیا، اور عام کا حکم مختلف فیہ ہے اس لئے اس کو تفصیل سے بیان کیا ۔ بہر حال خاص کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے مدلول پر قطعی اور یقینی طور پر اس طرح شامل ہوتا ہے کہ اس میں غیر کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا، جیسے ثلثة قروءمیں ثلثہ خاص ہے، یہ اپنے مدلول کو قطعی طور پر شامل ہے،ثلثہ کا اطلاق نہ تین سے کم پر ہوتا نہ تین سے زیادہ پر۔ اور عام کا حکم یہ ہے کہ وہ اپنے تمام افراد میں قطعی اور یقینی طور پر حکم کو واجب کرتا ہے ،جس طرح خاص قطعی ہوتا ہے، احناف کا مسلک یہی ہے، بعض حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ عام میں توقف کیا جائے گا جب تک کوئی دلیل معین قائم نہ ہو جائے ، يوجب الحکم کہہ کر مصنف نے اس کی تردید کی بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں عام اگر واحد کا صیغہ ہے تو ایک پر دلالت کرے گا اور جمع کا صیغہ ہے تو تین پر دلالت کرے گا اور باقی افراد میں توقف ہو گا دلیل قائم ہونے تک، فيما تناولہ سے مصنف نے اس کی تردید کردی ، امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک عام قطعی نہیں بلکہ ظنی ہے ، تو مصنف ان نے قطعاً ويقينا سے اس قول کی تردید کردی۔ الااذا لحقه :- سے مصنف یہ بتارہے ہیں کہ عام قطعی ہوتا ہے مگر کسی دلیل مخصص سے عام کے اندر اگر تخصیص ہو جائے تو پھر عام قطعی نہیں رہتا ہے، بلکہ ظنی ہو جاتا ہے، اس وقت وہ صرف حکم کو واجب کرتا ہے مگر اس احتمال کے ساتھ کہ جس دلیل سے پہلے کچھ افراد عام میں سے خاص کئے گئے ہیں ، ہوسکتا ہے کہ اس دلیل کے تحت عام کے کچھ اور افراد بھی آجائیں ، اور وہ بھی عام کے حکم سے خارج ہو جائیں جیسے اللہ تعالٰی کا ارشاد فا قتلوا المشركين مشرکین کو قتل کر وہ مشرکین عام ہے ، تمام مشرکین سے قتال کا حکم ہے، مگر وان احد من المشركين استجارك فاجرہ مشرکین میں سے کوئی پناہ مانگے تو پناہ دے دو، اس کے ذریعہ تخصیص ہو گئی یعنی امن طلب کرنے والے مشرکین سے خارج ہو گئے ، ان سے قتال نہیں کیا جائے گا اور نصوص میں اصل علت ہے ہم نے اس کی علت نکالی لڑائی سے عاجز ہونا‘ لہذا اس علت کی وجہ سے مشرکین میں سے عورتیں، بوڑھے، اپا نچ ، اندھے اور راہسبین سب کی تخصیص ہو گئی یعنی ان سے بھی قتال نہ ہوگا مخصص معلوم کی مثال ہے۔ الحاصل جب عام میں حصص معلوم یا مجہول کے ذریعے تخصیص ہو جائے گی تو عام اپنے باقی افراد میں عمل کو واجب کرے گا ظنیت کے ساتھ ۔ جیسے اللہ تعالی کا ارشاد احل الله البيع وحرم الربو میں بیچ لام استغراق داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے عام ہے، جو تمام بیوع کوحتی کہ ربو کو بھی شامل ہے، پھر حرم الربو کہہ کر بیع ربو کی تخصیص کی گئی یعنی بیع ربو حلال نہیں ہے یہ خصص مجہول ہے کیونکہ ربو کے معنی زیادتی ہے اور یہ معلوم نہیں کہ کون سی زیادتی مراد ہے ، یہاں مطلق زیادتی مراد نہیں ہے، کیونکہ بیچ بھی زیادتی اور نفع ہی کے لئے مشروع ہوتی ہے، اگر مطلق زیادتی حرام کہیں گے تو بیع کا دروازہ ہی بند ہو جائے گا ، معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی خاص زیادتی مراد ہے پس می خصص مجہول کی مثال ہوئی۔ مگر رسول اللہ صلی یا ایلیم نے چھ چیزوں سے اس کی تفسیر کر دی کہ گیہوں ، جو ، چھوہارے ،نمک ،سونا اور چاندی میں اگر بجنسہ بیع کی گئی یا کمی زیادتی کے ساتھ کی گئی تو یہ ربو ہے ، پس حضور صلی شما یک پیام کے تفسیر کرنے کے بعد حرم الربو مخصص معلوم بن گیا، اور مخصص معلوم کی طرح محتمل تعلیل ہو گیا حنفیہ نے قدرو جنس علت نکال کر چاول ہکئی وغیرہ کو بھی چھ چیزوں کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا، بہر حال عام تخصص سے پہلے قطعی ہوگا، تخصیص کے بعد ظنی ہوگا، چاہےمخصص معلوم ہو یا مجہول کیونکہ اگر مخصص معلوم ہے تو اس کی علت نکال کر عام کے باقی افراد میں بھی تخصیص کا احتمال رہے گا لہذا عام کے باقی افراد میں قطعیت نہیں رہے گی، اور اگر شخص مجهول ہے تو شارع کی طرف سے اس کی تفسیر کے بعد وہ معلوم ہوکر محتمل تعلیل ہو جائے گا۔
The author, after defining khas and amm, now states the ruling but only stated the ruling of amm and only indicated the ruling of khas by saying 'al-khas fi ma tana'waluh'. The reason is that the ruling of khas, according to the majority, is non-disputed, so it was only indicated. The ruling of amm is disputed, so it was stated in detail. In any case, the ruling of khas is that it includes its referent in a definitive and certain way such that there is no probability of other than it. Like 'thalathat quru' (three periods): 'thalathah' is khas, it includes its referent definitively; 'thalathah' does not apply to less than three nor more than three. And the ruling of amm is that it makes the ruling obligatory upon all its individuals in a definitive and certain way, just as khas is definitive. This is the position of the Hanafis. Some say that one should pause regarding amm until a specific evidence is established. By saying 'yujib al-hukm', the author refutes this. Some say that if amm is in the singular form, it indicates one, and if in plural form, it indicates three, and for the remaining individuals, there is pause until evidence is established. By 'fi ma tana'waluh', the author refutes this. According to Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him), amm is not definitive but conjectural. So the author refutes this with 'qat'an wa yaqinan'. 'Ila idha lahiqahu' means the author is explaining that amm is definitive, but if specification (takhsis) occurs within it by a specificatory evidence, then it is no longer definitive, but rather conjectural. At that time, it only makes the ruling obligatory with the probability that the evidence by which some individuals were previously specified may also include other individuals of the general, and they too may be excluded from the ruling of the general. Like Allah's statement: 'So kill the polytheists.' 'Polytheists' is general, it commands fighting all polytheists. But 'And if one of the polytheists seeks your protection, then grant him protection' specifies: those seeking protection are excluded, no fighting with them. And in the texts, there is an original cause; we extracted the cause: inability to fight. Hence, due to this cause, women, elderly, disabled, blind, and monks among the polytheists are also specified, i.e., no fighting with them. This is an example of a known specified. In summary, when specification occurs in the general through a known or unknown specificatory factor, the general makes the ruling obligatory upon its remaining individuals with conjecture. Like Allah's statement: 'Allah has permitted trade and prohibited usury.' 'Trade' due to the definite article for all-inclusiveness is general, including all trades, even usury. Then 'and prohibited usury' specifies trade of usury, i.e., trade of usury is not lawful. This is an example of an unknown specificatory factor because 'riba' means increase, and it is not known which increase is intended. Here absolute increase is not intended, because trade is also instituted for increase and profit. If we say absolute increase is prohibited, the door of trade would be closed. It becomes clear that a specific increase is intended. So this is an example of an unknown specifier. But the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) interpreted it with six items: wheat, barley, dates, salt, gold, and silver – if sold in kind with increase or deficit, that is riba. So after the interpretation by the Prophet (peace be upon him), 'prohibited usury' became a known specifier, and like a known specifier, it becomes susceptible to analogy. The Hanafis extracted the cause of measure and genus and attached rice, etc., to the six items. In any case, the general is definitive before specification, and after specification it becomes conjectural, whether the specifier is known or unknown, because if it is known, its cause can be extracted and there is probability of specification in other remaining individuals, so certainly is not maintained. And if it is unknown, after its interpretation by the Lawgiver, it becomes known and susceptible to analogy.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul ruling stating that the general term (amm), according to the Hanafi school, is definitive (qat'i) in indicating its ruling on all its individuals, unlike the Shafi'i view that it is conjectural (zanni). The author explains that specification (takhsis) does not destroy the definitiveness of the general for the remaining individuals; rather, it reduces it to conjecture because after specification, the general's remaining individuals may also be subject to further specification through analogy. Two Quranic examples are given: the verse 'kill the polytheists' which is general, then specified by the exception for those seeking protection, and further by qiyas (analogy) based on the cause of inability to fight, excluding women, elderly, etc. The second example is the verse 'Allah has permitted trade and prohibited usury,' where 'trade' is general and 'usury' is an unknown specifier until the Prophet (PBUH) specified it by listing the six ribawi items. After that, it becomes a known specifier but still allows for qiyas, thus the general remains conjectural. The lesson emphasizes that the Hanafi position is that amm is qat'i before takhsis and zanni after, countering other views that amm is always zanni or requires pause.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A general term that includes all its individuals without restriction; its ruling is qat'i on all individuals before specification.
خاص (khas): A specific term that definitively includes only its referent with no probability of others.
تخصیص (takhsis): The act of specifying or excepting some individuals from the general term, which changes the general from qat'i to zanni for the remaining individuals.
مخصص (mukhassis): The evidence that effects specification; it may be known (e.g., text) or unknown (e.g., cause) until interpreted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a general term (amm) after specification (takhsis) has occurred?
A) It becomes completely invalid and no longer indicates any ruling.
B) It remains qat'i (definitive) for the remaining individuals.
C) It becomes zanni (conjectural) for the remaining individuals.
D) It requires complete pause until a new evidence is found.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, amm is definitively binding before takhsis; after takhsis, it remains binding but with conjecture (zann), not invalidity.

Definition and Ruling of Mushtarak and Mu'awwal
Defines mushtarak and mu'awwal with their rulings and a Hanafi-Shafi'i example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mushtarak and mu'awwal, state their legal rulings, and apply the Hanafi approach to interpreting a mushtarak word.

Core Idea
A mushtarak word requires pause until interpreted; its interpretation (mu'awwal) binds action but not certainty.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, words are categorized by clarity. Among them, mushtarak (common) and mu'awwal (interpreted) are important because they guide how a mujtahid approaches ambiguous texts. This lesson will define both terms, explain their legal rulings, and show how Hanafis handle a mushtarak word like 'qar' in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of mushtarak
Mushtarak can be within the same category of meanings (e.g., 'qar' for both menstruation and purity) or across different external entities (e.g., 'mu'ayyan' for eye, spring, gold).
2
Understand the ruling of mushtarak
The ruling is tawaqquf (pause) – one must not act immediately but must deliberate until one meaning is determined by dominant conjecture.
3
See how mushtarak becomes mu'awwal
When a meaning is determined by dominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann), the word is called mu'awwal. It is binding but not certain.
4
Note the ruling and effect of mu'awwal
Action upon mu'awwal is obligatory, but it remains open to error. Hence, a denier of a mu'awwal interpretation is not considered a disbeliever.
5
Distinguish mu'awwal from definitive texts
Mu'awwal differs from muhkam (definitive) because it lacks certainty. The passage clarifies that mu'awwal here specifically arises from mushtarak, not from other ambiguous categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي ۲۱ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي قر حیض اور طہر کے معنی میں مشترک ہے، دوم وہ جس میں مسمیات و افراد کا یعنی اعیان خارجیہ کا اشتراک ہوتا ہے جیسے لفظ معین آنکھ، آفتاب چشمه، گھنٹہ، سونا، کشتی و غیره اعیان خارجیہ کے درمیان مشترک ہے۔ مشترک کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس میں توقف کیا جائے تا کہ اس میں غور و فکر کر کے اس کا کوئی ایک معنی متعین ہو جائے ، جب ایک معنی متعین ہو جائے تو اس کو ترجیح حاصل ہوگی اور اسی پر اعتقاد اور عمل واجب ہوگا جیسے لفظ قر ، حیض وطہر کے معنی میں ہے، احناف نے غور وفکر کر کے حیض کے معنی مراد لئے ، اور شوافع نے طہر کے معنی ، پھر مشترک میں جب ظن غالب سے ایک معنی متعین ہو گئے تو اب اس کو مؤول کہیں گے، اور مؤول کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اس پر عمل تو واجب ہے مگر غلطی کے احتمال کے ساتھ، یعنی مجتہد کی تاویل سے جو معنی متعین ہوئے ہیں ، ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ معنی صحیح نہ ہو بیچ دوسرا معنی ہو، پس مؤول مؤجب عمل تو ہے مگر موجب یقین نہیں ہے، اسی لئے اس کا منکر کا فرنہیں ہوگا ما ترجح من المشترك مؤول کی تعریف میں مشترک کا لفظ بڑھا کر یہ بتانا چاہتے ہیں کہ یہ مؤول سے وہ مؤول مراد ہے جو مشترک سے پیدا ہوتا ہے، ورنہ خفی ، مشکل، اور مجمل کا بھی جب خفا دور ہو جائے تو اس کو بھی مؤول کہتے ہیں مگر وہ بیان کے اقسام میں سے ہے۔
Al-Faid al-Hijazi 21 Sharh Urdu al-Muntakhab al-Husami. The word 'qar' is common between menstruation and purity. Second, the one in which meanings and individuals i.e. external entities share, like the word 'mu'ayyan' is common among eye, sun, spring, hour, gold, boat, etc. external entities. The ruling of the common (mushtarak) is that one must pause in it, until after deliberation one meaning is determined. When one meaning is determined, it will have preference and belief and action upon it is obligatory, like the word 'qar' is between the meanings of menstruation and purity. The Hanafis, after deliberation, took the meaning of menstruation, and the Shafi'is the meaning of purity. Then, in the common, when one meaning is determined by prevalent conjecture, it is called mu'awwal. The ruling of mu'awwal is that action upon it is obligatory but with the possibility of error, meaning the meaning determined by the mujtahid's interpretation may not be correct and the other meaning might be correct. So mu'awwal necessitates action but does not necessitate certainty. Therefore, its denier is not a disbeliever. By adding the word 'common' in the definition of mu'awwal, they intend to show that mu'awwal here refers to that which arises from the common. Otherwise, khafi, mushkil, and mujmal, when their obscurity is removed, are also called mu'awwal, but that is from the types of bayan.
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage defines two key usul terms: mushtarak (common/ambiguous word) and mu'awwal (interpreted word). The author states that mushtarak is a word that has multiple meanings, either in the same class (like 'qar' meaning both menstruation and purity) or across different external entities (like 'mu'ayyan' meaning eye, spring, etc.). The ruling for mushtarak is that it requires deliberation (tawaqquf) until one meaning is determined. Once a meaning is preferred, belief and action become obligatory upon that meaning. The Hanafis and Shafi'is differ on the meaning of 'qar' in the Quranic verse about divorce: Hanafis take it as menstruation, Shafi'is as purity. When a meaning is determined by dominant conjecture, the word becomes mu'awwal. The ruling of mu'awwal is that action is obligatory, but it does not produce certainty—it is open to error. Hence, denying a mu'awwal interpretation does not amount to disbelief. The author clarifies that mu'awwal in this context specifically arises from mushtarak; other ambiguous categories like khafi, mushkil, and mujmal, when clarified, are also called mu'awwal but belong to the types of bayan (clarification). This is a typical Hanafi definition emphasizing the probabilistic nature of interpretation.

Key Terms
مشترک (mushtarak): A word that has more than one meaning, either in the same category (like 'qar' for menstruation and purity) or across different entities (like 'mu'ayyan' meaning eye, spring, etc.).
مؤول (mu'awwal): A mushtarak word after one meaning is determined by dominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann); it is binding but not certain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Action is obligatory immediately
B) One must pause (tawaqquf) and deliberate
C) It is considered muhkam
D) It is invalid

Key Takeaway
Mushtarak words require pause and ijtihad; their interpreted meanings (mu'awwal) are binding for action but do not produce certainty.

Haqiqah, Majaz, Sarih, Kinayah: Two Axes of Word Classification
Explaining the third classification of words: usage and clarity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any word on two independent axes: usage (haqiqah vs. majaz) and clarity (sarih vs. kinayah), and apply this to Quranic expressions.

Core Idea
Haqiqah/majaz and sarih/kinayah are two separate divisions: usage versus clarity.

This passage refines the standard classification of words in usul al-fiqh. The author introduces a second criterion—'flow' or 'clarity'—alongside 'usage' to create two independent divisions. This avoids the conceptual overlap that would occur if all four types were treated as mutually exclusive parts of a single division. Understanding this duality is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two criteria
The passage uses 'usage' (istimal) and 'flow' (jaryan) as two separate bases for classifying words. Write down each criterion and what it asks about the word.
Usage asks: is the word used in its original meaning? Flow asks: is the meaning expressed explicitly or by implication?
2
Define haqiqah and majaz based on usage
Haqiqah = word used in its wad'i (original) meaning. Majaz = word used in a non-wad'i meaning with a qarinah (contextual indicator).
Example: 'lion' used for a brave man is majaz.
3
Define sarih and kinayah based on clarity
Sarih = word whose meaning is clear and explicit without context. Kinayah = word that hints at a meaning through implication, requiring external context.
Example: 'He has a long hand' is kinayah for generosity, but 'hand' is used in its literal sense (haqiqah).
4
Recognize the two divisions are independent
The author emphasizes that these four types are not one division but two. This avoids the objection that sarih/kinayah can combine with haqiqah/majaz.
Thus, a word can be haqiqah sarih, haqiqah kinayah, majaz sarih, or majaz kinayah.
5
Apply to a Quranic example
Take a word from the Quran and classify it on both axes. For instance, 'yad' (hand) in 'yadu Allahi fawqa aydihim' (48:10): is it haqiqah or majaz? Sarih or kinayah?
Hanafis often treat 'yad' as majaz (power) and kinayah (implied meaning).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ فِي وُجُوْهِ اِسْتِعْمَالِ ذَلِكَ النَّظْمِ وَجَرَيَانِهِ فِي بَابِ الْبَيَانِ وَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ الْحَقِيْقَةُ وَالْمَجَازُ وَالصَّرِيحُ وَالْكِنَايَةُ ترجمہ:۔ اور تیسری تقسیم بیان معنی کے باب میں اس نظم کے استعمال اور اس کے جاری ہونے کی قسموں میں ہے اور وہ چار ہیں حقیقت مجاز ، صریح ، کنایہ۔ تشریح : - کتاب اللہ کی چار تقسیموں میں سے دو بیان ہو چکیں، تیسری تقسیم شروع کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ جو معنی پر دلالت کرتا ہے اس کی تیسری تقسیم اس لفظ کے استعمال اور اس کے جریان کے اعتبار سے ہے، استعمال یعنی وہ لفظ معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل ہے یا معنی غیر موضوع لہ میں ، اول حقیقت اور ثانی مجاز ہے، اور جریان کا مطلب ہے کہ وہ لفظ بیان وظہور معنی کے باب میں کس طرح جاری ہے ، بیان معنی میں انکشاف ووضوح ہے یا استنتار ہے،اول صریح اور ثانی کنایہ ہے۔ مصنف عالیہ نے استعمال اور جریان دو لفظ ذکر کئے ، حالانکہ صاحب منار وغیرہ نے استعمال کے لفظ پر اکتفا کیا ہے، جریان کا اضافہ نہیں کیا ہے ، مصنف نے یہ اضافہ ایک اشکال سے بچنے کے لیے کیا ہے کہ ان چار قسموں یعنی حقیقت ، مجاز، صریح، کنایہ میں تبائین نہیں ہے بلکہ صریح اور کنایہ حقیقت کے ساتھ بھی جمع ہو جاتے ہیں اور مجاز کے ساتھ بھی ، یعنی حقیقت صریح، حقیقت کنایہ اور مجاز صریح، مجاز کنایہ، حالانکہ ایک تقسیم کے اقسام میں تبائین ہونا چاہیے، اقسام آپس میں جمع نہ ہونی چاہئیں، تو اس اشکال سے بچنے کے لئے ، استعمال اور جریان دو لفظ استعمال کئے ، اور فرمایا کہ یہ چار اقسام ایک تقسیم کی نہیں ہیں، بلکہ دو تقسیم کی ہیں، ایک استعمال لفظ کی تقسیم ہے جس کی دو قسمیں حقیقت و مجاز ہیں اور
And the third division is regarding the ways of usage of that composition and its flow in the chapter of bayan, and they are four: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, and kinayah. Translation: And the third division is regarding the ways of usage of that composition and its flow in the chapter of bayan, and they are four: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, and kinayah. Explanation: Two of the four divisions of the Book of Allah have been explained. Now the third division is begun. He says that the third division of words in terms of indication of meaning is based on the usage (istimal) of the word and its flow (jaryan). Usage means whether the word is used in its original meaning (ma‘na mawdu‘ lahu) or in a transferred meaning (ghayr mawdu‘ lahu); the first is haqiqah, the second is majaz. And flow means how the word flows in the chapter of bayan and clarity of meaning: whether it is clear and explicit (inkishaf wa wuduh) or hidden (istitar); the first is sarih, the second is kinayah. The author (musannif) mentioned both 'usage' and 'flow' although the author of al-Manar and others sufficed with the word 'usage' and did not add 'flow'. The author added this to avoid an objection: these four types (haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah) are not mutually exclusive; rather, sarih and kinayah can combine with haqiqah and also with majaz, i.e., haqiqah sarih, haqiqah kinayah, and majaz sarih, majaz kinayah. However, the parts of a single division should be mutually exclusive and should not combine. To avoid this objection, the author used two words ('usage' and 'flow') and said that these four types are not from one division but from two divisions: one is the division of usage of the word, whose two types are haqiqah and majaz, and [the sentence cuts off].
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage introduces the third classification of Quranic expressions: haqiqah (literal), majaz (metaphorical), sarih (explicit), and kinayah (allusive). The key insight is that these are not four types of one division but rather two separate divisions: haqiqah vs. majaz (based on usage: whether the word is used in its original meaning or not) and sarih vs. kinayah (based on clarity: whether the meaning is clearly expressed or hinted). The author of this commentary (likely the author of al-Fayd al-Hijazi) points out that combining them into one division would lead to overlap (e.g., a word can be haqiqah and kinayah, like 'he has a long hand' meaning generosity). To avoid this, the author (musannif) distinguishes between 'usage' and 'flow' as two separate criteria. This is a refinement over earlier works like al-Manar which used only 'usage'. Thus, a word can be analyzed on two axes: literal/metaphorical and explicit/allusive. This precision prevents confusion in legal interpretation, where a text's classification affects its legal force. For example, a kinayah may require additional context for a legal ruling.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): A word used in its original (wad‘i) meaning, as per the linguistic convention.
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a meaning other than its original, with a contextual indicator (qarinah) that prevents the literal meaning.
صریح (sarih): A word whose meaning is clear and explicit, without need for external context.
کنایہ (kinayah): A word that hints at a meaning through implication, requiring context to determine the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author of this passage add the term 'jaryan' (flow) alongside 'istimal' (usage)?
A) To indicate that words can flow in speech
B) To avoid the objection that haqiqah, majaz, sarih, kinayah are not mutually exclusive under one division
C) To show that kinayah is better than sarih
D) To limit the classification to only two types

Key Takeaway
Words are classified by two independent criteria: usage (haqiqah vs. majaz) and clarity (sarih vs. kinayah), yielding four possible combinations.

The Two-Class System of Word Usage: Haqiqah/Majaz and Sarih/Kinayah
Defining haqiqah and majaz and explaining the need for two separate classifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given word as haqiqah or majaz based on usage, and as sarih or kinayah based on clarity, and explain why these are two independent axes.

Core Idea
Haqiqah and majaz categorize usage; sarih and kinayah categorize clarity — two separate axes that do not overlap.

In Usul al-Fiqh, understanding how words convey meaning is essential for interpreting legal texts. This lesson introduces four key terms: haqiqah (literal), majaz (figurative), sarih (explicit), and kinayah (allusive). The passage explains why these form two separate classifications — one based on the word's usage (isti'mal) and one on the flow of expression (jaryan) — to avoid logical overlap.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the fourth division of word-study
The chapter of bayan (expression) lists haqiqah, majaz, sarih, and kinayah as aspects of word usage and flow.
This division is part of the broader classification of words in usul.
2
Identify the danger of a single classification
If all four belong to one division, sarih and kinayah would overlap with haqiqah and majaz, since a word can be both haqiqah and sarih, or both majaz and kinayah.
Overlap (ijtima') leads to confusion in legal interpretation.
3
Separate the two axes
The author solves this by making two independent classifications: isti'mal (usage) for haqiqah/majaz, and jaryan (flow) for sarih/kinayah.
Now a word belongs to one category from each axis without conflict.
4
Define haqiqah
A word used for its original meaning (ma wudi'a lahu).
Haqiqah is the default mode of usage.
5
Define majaz
A word used for a meaning other than its original due to a connection (ittisal), either meaning-based (ma'navi) or formal (suri).
Examples: calling a brave person 'lion' (meaning-connection) or rain 'sky' (formal connection).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْقِسْمُ الثَّالِثُ فِي وُجُوْهِ اِسْتِعْمَالِ ذَلِكَ النَّظْمِ وَجَرَيَانِهِ فِي بَابِ الْبَيَانِ وَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ الْحَقِيْقَةُ وَالْمَجَازُ وَالصَّرِيحُ وَالْكِنَايَةُ. فَالْحَقِيْقَةُ اِسْمْ لِكُلِّ لَفْظِ أُرِيْدَ بِهِ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ وَالْمَجَازُ اسْمْ لِكُلِّ لَفْظِ أُرِيْدَ بِهِ غَيْرُ مَاوُضِعَ لَهُ لِاِتِّصَالٍ بَيْنَهُمَا مَعْنَى كَمَا فِي تَسْمِيَةِ الشَّجَاعَ أَسَدًا وَالْبَلِيْدِ حِمَارًا أَوْذَاتَا كَمَا فِي تَسْمِيَةِ الْمَطَرِ سَمَاء وَالْإِيصَالُ سَبَبًا مِنْ هَذَا الْقَبِيْلِ وَهُوَ نَوْعَانِ
And the third division is regarding the aspects of usage of that arrangement and its flow in the chapter of expression, and they are four: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, and kinayah. So haqiqah is a name for every word by which is intended what it was placed for, and majaz is a name for every word by which is intended other than what it was placed for, due to a connection between them, either a meaning-connection as in calling the brave a lion and the dull-witted a donkey, or a self-connection as in calling rain 'sky', and the connection is a cause of this kind, and it is of two types.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the third classification of words in usul al-fiqh: the division based on usage (isti'mal) and flow (jaryan) in the chapter of bayan (expression). The author, following the matn, states that there are four categories: haqiqah (literal), majaz (figurative), sarih (explicit), and kinayah (allusive). However, to avoid the logical problem that sarih and kinayah can combine with haqiqah and majaz (e.g., a word can be both haqiqah and sarih, or haqiqah and kinayah), the author distinguishes between two separate classifications: one based on isti'mal (usage in original or transferred meaning) giving haqiqah and majaz, and another based on jaryan (clarity or hiddenness in expression) giving sarih and kinayah. Thus, there is no overlap between the two pairs. Then the passage defines haqiqah as a word used for its original meaning (ma wudi'a lahu), and majaz as a word used for a meaning other than its original, provided there is a connection (ittisal) between the two meanings. The connection can be ma'navi (meaning-based) as in calling a brave person a lion (shuja'a asad) due to shared trait of bravery, or suri (formal/self-based) as in calling rain 'sama' (sky) because rain comes from the sky. The author notes that the connection is a cause (sabab) and it is of two types, which he will elaborate as ma'navi and suri.

Key Terms
الحقيقة (al-ḥaqīqah): A word used for the meaning it was originally placed for.
المجاز (al-majāz): A word used for a meaning other than its original, due to a connection.
الصريح (aṣ-ṣarīḥ): An explicit word that clearly conveys its meaning without ambiguity.
الكناية (al-kināyah): An allusive word that hints at a meaning without explicit mention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason the author uses two separate classifications (isti'mal and jaryan) instead of one for the four terms?
A) To simplify the definitions.
B) To avoid the problem that sarih and kinayah can combine with haqiqah and majaz.
C) Because the matn uses different terms.
D) To emphasize the importance of majaz.

Key Takeaway
Haqiqah/majaz and sarih/kinayah are two independent axes: the former based on usage, the latter on clarity; they do not conflict.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Bidirectional Isti'ara: The Mutual Connection Between Cause and Ruling
Explains the strong connection between cause and effect for isti'ara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits isti'ara from both sides when the connection between cause and ruling is mutual, and apply this rule to new examples.

Core Idea
When cause and ruling are mutually dependent, figurative usage works both ways.

This lesson explores a key distinction in Hanafi usul: the difference between the mutual connection of illa and hukm versus the one-sided connection of sabab and musabbab. Through a rational proof, the author establishes when metaphorical language flows in both directions. Understanding this rule is essential for deriving rulings from cause-effect relationships in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two types of ittisal
Identify from the passage the two types of connection (ittisal) mentioned: ittisal sababi (cause-effect) and ittisal illi (cause-ruling). Focus on the latter, where the relationship is mutual.
The passage explains that ittisal suri includes both, but the author only discusses two subtypes: sabab-musabbab and illa-ma'lul.
2
Analyze the rational proof for mutual dependency
Examine the statement: 'because the cause was not legislated except for its ruling, and the ruling is not established except by a cause.' This demonstrates that the connection is equal and symmetric.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof); it is considered qati' in both transmission and meaning.
3
Apply the rule to the example of conditional manumission
Work through the example: 'If I buy a slave, he is free.' The second half becomes free because 'purchase' (cause) is used figuratively to mean 'ownership' (effect). Contrast with the case where the condition is 'If I own', which requires full ownership.
The example shows that isti'ara from cause to effect is valid, but from effect to cause is not unless the effect is specific to the cause.
