فرماتے ہیں کہ مطلق مقید پر محمول ہوگا یعنی کفارہ قتل میں مومن رقبہ ہے تو کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین میں بھی مومن رقبہ مراد ہوگا ، کیونکہ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ وصف شرط کے درجہ میں ہوتا ہے اور جس طرح شرط کے انتفاء سے حکم منتفی ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی وصف کے انتفاء سے حکم منتفی ہوتا ہے، لہذا منصوص علیہ یعنی کفارہ قتل میں اگر وصف نہ ہو یعنی رقبہ مومنہ نہ ہو تو کفارہ بھی نہیں ہے، تو منصوص علیہ پر غیر منصوص علیہ یعنی کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین کو بھی قیاس کرینگے اور وصف یہاں بھی ملحوظ ہو گا کیونکہ سب کی جنس ایک ہی ہے یعنی کفارہ ہونا اور مقصد بھی ایک ہے، اس کی مشروعیت ستر اور زجر کے لئے ہوئی ہے۔ وَعِنْدَنَا لَا يُحْمَلُ الْمُطْلَقُ عَلَى الْمُقْتَدِ وَأَنْ كَانَا حَادِثَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ بَعْدَ أَنْ يَكُونَا فِي الله. حُكْمَيْنِ لا مَكَانِ الْعَمَلِ بِهِمَا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ ، وَمُحَمَّدٌ فِيْمَنُ قَرِبَ الَّتِي ظَاهَرَ مِنْهَا فِي خِلَالِ الصَّوْمِ لَيْلاً عَامِدًا اَوْنَهَارًا نَاسِيَا إِنَّهُ لَيَسْتَأْنِفْ وَلَوْقَرَبَهَا فِي خِلَالِ الْإِطْعَامِ لَمْ يَسْتَأْنِفْ لِاَنَ شَرْطَ الْاِخْلَاءِ عَنِ الْمَسِيْسِ مِنْ ضَرُوْرَةِ شَرْطَ التَّقْدِيمِ عَلَى الْمَسِيْسِ وَذَلِكَ مَنْصُوصٌ عَلَيْهِ فِي الْاَعْتَاقِ وَالصِيَامِ دُونَ الْإِطْعَامِ ترجمہ: اور ہمارے نزدیک مقید پر محمول نہ ہوگا اگر چہ دونوں ایک حادثہ میں ہوں، بعد اس کے کہ وہ دونوں دو حکموں میں ہوں ، ان دونوں پر عمل کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے ، امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد اللہ نے فرمایا اس شخص کے بارے میں جس نے اس عورت سے جماع کیا جس سے ظہار کیا ہے روزہ کے دوران میں رات کو قصد آیا دن میں بھول کر کہ وہ از سر نو روزہ رکھے گا، اور اگر اس نے عورت سے جماع کیا اطعام کے درمیان تو استیناف نہیں کرے گا، اس لیے کہ جماع سے خالی کرنے کی شرط جماع پر (کفارہ کو ) مقدم کرنے کی شرط کی ضرورت میں سے ہے، اور تقدیم منصوص علیہ ہے اعتاق اور صیام میں نہ کہ اطعام میں ۔ ریح : - ہمارے نزدیک اگر مطلق اور مقید پر الگ الگ عمل کرنا ممکن ہو تو مطلق کو مقید پر محمول نہیں کرینگے ، چاہے ایک ہی واقعہ ہو یا الگ الگ مگر حکم دو ہوں جن پر الگ الگ عمل ممکن ہو تو مطلق اپنے طلاق پر رہے گا، کیونکہ دو حکموں میں ایک کو مطلق اور دوسرے کو مقید کرنے میں شارع کی حکمتیں وابستہ ہوتی ہیں، جو مطلق کو مقید پر محمول کرنے سے فوت ہو جاتی ہیں، جیسے حکم کو مقید کر کے سختی کرنا اور حکم کو مطلق رکھ کے نرمی کرنا وغیرہ لہذا جب دونوں پر اپنے اپنے طور سے عمل ممکن ہو تو مطلق کو مقید پر محمول نہیں کرینگے۔ مصنف سے طرفین کے حوالہ سے مثال ذکر کرتے ہیں کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے روزوں سے کفارہ ادا کرنے کے دوران بیوی سے جماع کر لیا تو اس کو از سر نو روزے رکھنا ضروری ہوگا، کیونکہ من قبل ان يتما سا کی قید لگی ہوئی ہے، اور اگر اطعام سے کفارہ ادا کر رہا ہے اور کچھ مسکینوں کو کھلانے کے بعد بیوی سے جماع کر لیا، تو استیناف نہیں کرے گا یعنی از سر نو سب کو کھانا نہیں کھلانا پڑے گا ، کیونکہ اطعام میں من قبل ان يتماسا کی قید نہیں ہے، تو دیکھئے واقعہ ایک ہی ہے یعنی ظہار مگر حکم الگ الگ ہیں کیونکہ کفارہ ظہار میں تین حکم ہیں (۱) اعتاق (۲) صیام (۳) اطعام - پہلے دو میں من قبل ان یتماسا کی قید ہے اور تیسرے میں نہیں ہے ، لہذا مطلق کو مقید پر محمول نہیں کرینگے، کیونکہ مطلق کو مطلق رکھ کر اور مقید کو مقید رکھ کر عمل ممکن ہے۔ لان شرط الاخلاء - سے مصنف دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ من قبل ان يتماسا کہہ کر کفارہ کو جماع پر مقدم کرنا شرط قرار دیا اور جب جماع پر کفارہ مقدم ہوا تو اس کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کفارہ جماع سے خالی ہو، کیونکہ اگر کفارہ جماع سے خالی نہ ہوگا تو وہ جماع پر مقدم نہ ہو سکے گا کیونکہ بیچ میں جماع ہو گیا پس کفارہ کو جماع پر مقدم کرنے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ جماع سے خالی ہو اور یہ مقدم کرنا منصوص ہے۔ اعتاق اور صیام میں ، نہ کہ اطعام میں، لہذا صیام میں اگر دوران میں جماع ہو گیا تو استیناف کرنا پڑے گا کیونکہ تقدیم فوت ہورہی ہے اور اطعام میں اگر دوران میں جماع ہوا تو استیناف نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں حکم مطلق ہے تقدیم کی شرط نہیں ہے۔ فائدہ :- عبارت میں لیلا کے بعد عامداً کی قید اتفاقی ہے کیونکہ رات میں عمد اجماع کرنا اور ناسیا دونوں برابر ہیں، اور نہارا کے بعد ناسیا کی قید احترازی ہے کیونکہ عمداً اگر کر لیا تو تابع صیام فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے بالا تفاق استیناف واجب ہوگا۔
To free a slave, to fast two consecutive months, to feed sixty poor people: the first two are restricted: 'free a slave before they touch each other' - 'and whoever does not find then fast two consecutive months before they touch each other' - meaning free a slave before intercourse, fast two months before intercourse. And the third is absolute: 'feed sixty poor people' - here the restriction 'before they touch each other' is absent. So Imam Shafi'i says that this absolute is carried upon the two restricted ones, so in this also the restriction of before intercourse will remain. Here the absolute and restricted are in one incident, which is zihar. If they are in separate incidents, its example is like kaffarah for murder, kaffarah for zihar, kaffarah for oath: these are separate incidents; in all three there is a ruling to free a slave, but in kaffarah for murder the slave is restricted: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake then free a believing slave', and in kaffarah for zihar and kaffarah for oath the slave is absolute like 'free a slave' and 'or free a slave'. Imam Shafi'i says that the absolute is carried upon the restricted, meaning in kaffarah for murder the slave is believing, so in kaffarah for zihar and kaffarah for oath also a believing slave is intended. Because Imam Shafi'i says that a description is like a condition, and just as the ruling is negated by the negation of a condition, similarly the ruling is negated by the negation of a description. Therefore in the specified case (mansus alayh), i.e., kaffarah for murder, if the description is absent, i.e., the slave is not believing, then there is no kaffarah. So upon the specified case we also analogize (qiyas) the non-specified cases, i.e., kaffarah for zihar and kaffarah for oath, and the description will be considered here too because all are of the same genus, i.e., being kaffarah, and the purpose is also one: its legislation is for veiling and deterrence. And according to us, the absolute is not carried upon the restricted even if both are in one incident, after they are in two rulings, because acting upon both is possible. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said concerning the one who had intercourse with the wife from whom he had done zihar during the fasting, intentionally at night or forgetfully by day that he must restart. And if he had intercourse during the feeding, he does not restart, because the condition of being free from touching is necessitated by the condition of preceding the touching, and that is specified in emancipation and fasting, not in feeding. Translation: And according to us, it will not be carried upon the restricted even if both are in one incident, after they are two rulings, due to the possibility of acting upon both. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said concerning the person who had intercourse with the wife from whom he had done zihar during the fast, intentionally at night or forgetfully by day, that he will restart the fast. And if he had intercourse during the feeding, he will not restart, because the condition of being free from contact is necessitated by the condition of preceding the contact, and that preceding is specified in emancipation and fasting, not in feeding. Explanation: According to us, if acting upon the absolute and the restricted separately is possible, we do not carry the absolute upon the restricted, whether it is one incident or separate, but the rulings are two, upon which separate action is possible. Then the absolute remains upon its absoluteness, because in two rulings, making one absolute and the other restricted involves wisdoms of the Lawgiver, which are lost by carrying the absolute upon the restricted, like making the ruling hard by restricting it and making it easy by keeping it absolute, etc. Therefore, when acting upon both in their own way is possible, we do not carry the absolute upon the restricted. The author mentions an example from both sides: if the one who did zihar had intercourse with his wife while performing the kaffarah by fasting, he must restart the fast, because the restriction 'before they touch' is attached. And if he is performing the kaffarah by feeding and after feeding some poor people he had intercourse, he will not restart, i.e., he does not have to feed all again from the beginning, because in feeding there is no restriction 'before they touch'. So see, the incident is one, i.e., zihar, but the rulings are separate, because in zihar kaffarah there are three rulings: (1) emancipation, (2) fasting, (3) feeding. The first two have the restriction 'before they touch', and the third does not. Therefore we do not carry the absolute upon the restricted, because acting with the absolute as absolute and the restricted as restricted is possible. From 'because the condition of being free' the author is giving the proof: by saying 'before they touch', making the kaffarah precede intercourse is made a condition. And when kaffarah precedes intercourse, it is necessary that the kaffarah be free of intercourse, because if the kaffarah is not free of intercourse, it cannot precede intercourse since intercourse occurred in between. So for kaffarah to precede intercourse it is necessary that it be free of intercourse, and this preceding is specified in emancipation and fasting, not in feeding. Therefore in fasting, if intercourse occurs during it, he must restart because the sequence is lost, and in feeding, if intercourse occurs during it, he does not restart because the ruling there is absolute, there is no condition of preceding. Benefit: In the phrase, 'at night' the word 'intentionally' is coincidental, because at night intentional intercourse and forgetful are equal. And 'by day' the word 'forgetfully' is precautionary, because if done intentionally, then due to the expiration of the fasting sequence, by agreement restart is obligatory.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a discussion on the usul principle of carrying the absolute (mutlaq) to the restricted (muqayyad). It presents the Shafi'i position that when an absolute and a restricted provision occur in the same context (e.g., the same incident of zihar), the absolute is carried to the restricted. The Hanafi position, as per Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, is that if both the absolute and the restricted can be practically applied separately (i.e., the rulings are distinct), then they are not carried. The example is from the kaffarah of zihar: the Quran mentions in surah al-Mujadilah (58:3-4) that one must free a slave before intercourse, or if unable, fast two consecutive months before intercourse, but the third option (feeding sixty poor people) is mentioned without the restriction 'before intercourse'. Shafi'i argues that the restriction applies to all because the incident is one. Hanafi argues that since the rulings are separate (emancipation, fasting, feeding) and each can be practiced independently (the restriction is explicitly mentioned for the first two, omitted for the third), there is no need to carry the absolute to the restricted. The text also provides the ruling: if one who is doing kaffarah by fasting has intercourse, he must restart the fast because the condition of preceding is lost; but if one is doing feeding, intercourse does not require restarting. The benefit at the end clarifies that in the wording, 'intentionally' at night is included even though it is the same as forgetful, but for daytime 'forgetful' is specified because intentional would break the fast anyway.

Key Terms
مطلق (mutlaq): A word that indicates its meaning without any restriction or condition, e.g., 'slave' without specifying believing.
مقید (muqayyad): A word that indicates its meaning with a restriction or condition, e.g., 'believing slave'.
حمل المطلق على المقيد (haml al-mutlaq 'ala al-muqayyad): The principle of interpreting an absolute expression in light of a restricted one from the same context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a person performs zihar and then has intercourse while performing the kaffarah by feeding sixty poor people?
A) He must restart the feeding from the beginning.
B) He does not restart; he continues from where he left off.
C) He must also fast two months instead.
D) He must repeat all three options.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the absoluteness of a text when the restriction is absent, provided both the absolute and restricted can be independently enacted.

Specifying the General by Its Cause in Hanafi Usul
Presents a maxim about specifying the general by its cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on specification of a general term by its cause and apply it to distinguish between cases where the general is specified and where it remains general.

Core Idea
A general text is specified by its cause only if no other general text conflicts.

When a Quranic verse or hadith was revealed about a specific incident, does its general wording apply to all similar cases or only to that incident? The Hanafi school has a nuanced principle: the general is specified by its cause, but only in the absence of another general text that would keep it general. This lesson unpacks that rule and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The passage contrasts 'what some said' (the opposing view) with 'according to us' (the Hanafi view). Identify each party and their claim.
Opposing view: general is not specified by its cause. Hanafi view: it is specified, but with a condition.
2
Extract the Hanafi condition
The Arabic 'idha lam' indicates a conditional clause. Determine what condition is implied by the context. The full rule is: the general is specified by its cause unless there is another general text that prevents specification.
The passage cuts off, but the commentary confirms the condition.
3
Apply the rule to an example
Consider a verse revealed about a specific person. Under the Hanafi rule, if the verse is truly general in wording, but its cause is specific, it applies only to that cause unless a parallel general verse exists. Apply the rule to determine the scope.
Example: the verse of zihar (Q. 58:2-4) was revealed about a specific woman, but Hanafis hold it general for all cases because no conflicting general exists.
4
Contrast with the opposing school
The opposing school would maintain the general application regardless of the cause. Understand the thamarah (practical difference) between the two positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا مَا قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ اِنَ الْعَامَ يَخْصُّ بِسَبَبِهِ وَعِنْدَنَا إِنَّمَا يَخُصُّ بِسَبَبِهِ إِذا لَمْ
And among them is what some said: The general is specified by its cause. And according to us (Hanafis), it is specified by its cause only if not...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage introduces a dispute about the specification of a general term ('aam) by its specific cause (sabab). The author reports the view of some scholars (likely the Shafi'is or others) that when a general statement is made in connection with a specific cause, it remains general unless there is evidence to the contrary. In contrast, the Hanafi position (indana) is that the general term is indeed specified by its cause, but only if there is no other evidence (such as a separate general text) that would prevent that specification. The text cuts off mid-sentence, so the complete Hanafi principle is that the general is specified by its cause unless there is another general that conflicts (as in the famous rule: 'al-'aam yukhsas bi sababihi 'indana illa idha kana al-'aam mu'aran' or similar). This is a foundational principle in Hanafi usul affecting how verses revealed about specific incidents (asbab al-nuzul) or hadiths with specific contexts are interpreted.

Key Terms
العام (al-'aam): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
السبب (al-sabab): The specific cause or occasion for a ruling.
يخص (yukhsas): To specify; to restrict the general to a particular instance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: a general text is specified by its cause, but only if no other general text conflicts; otherwise the general remains general.

The Usul Dispute: Is al-'Amm Specified by Its Cause of Revelation?
Presenting the dispute over whether a general statement is confined to its specific occasion of revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether a general statement is specified by its specific cause of revelation, differentiate it from the Shafi'i view, and apply this principle to Quranic verses revealed about specific individuals.

Core Idea
A general statement is not confined to its specific occasion; it remains general unless explicit specification is proven.

One of the key usul disputes concerns the effect of the cause of revelation (sabab al-wurud) on the scope of a general statement (al-amm). Some schools argue that if a general verse was revealed about a particular person or incident, it applies only to that context. The Hanafi school, however, insists that the default is generality ('umum) and that the specific cause does not limit the ruling unless the expression is inherently dependent. In this lesson, we unpack this dispute and examine the evidence from the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two opposing views: the view that 'amm is specified by its cause, and the Hanafi view that it is not.
2
Define the Hanafi exceptions
Learn the three cases where the Hanafis do accept specification: non-independent expressions (na'am/bala), conditional contexts (jaza'), and responses (jawab).
3
Examine the opposing evidence
Consider the opposing school's argument: since the utterance was occasioned by a specific cause, it should be limited to that case.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand the Hanafi response: the Companions universally applied such verses (Zihar, Li'an, Qadhf, Sariqa), showing that the default is generality.
5
Apply to examples
Work through the Quranic examples to see the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) in deriving rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنْهَا مَا قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ اِنَ الْعَامَ يَخْصُّ بِسَبَبِهِ وَعِنْدَنَا إِنَّمَا يَخُصُّ بِسَبَبِهِ إِذا لَمْ يَكُنْ مُسْتَقِلاً بِنَفْسِهِ كَقَوْلِهِ نَعَمْ أَوْ بَلَى اَوْ خَرَجَ مُخْرَجَ الْجَزَاءِ كَقَوْلِ الرَّاوِى سَهَا رَسُوْلُ اللهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَسَجَدَ اَوْ خَرَجَ مُخْرَجَ الْجَوَابَ كَالْمُدْعُو إِلَى الْغَدَاءِ وَيَقُولُ وَاللَّهِ لَا اَتَغَدَى فَأَمَا إِذَازَادَ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْجَوَابِ فَقَالَ وَاللهِ لَا اَتَغَدَى الْيَوْمَ وَهُوَ مَوْضِعُ الْخِلَافِ فَعِنْدَنَا يَصِيْرُ مُبْتَدِأُ احْتَرَارًا عَنْ أَلْغَاءِ الزِّيَادَةِ ترجمہ: اور ان وجوہ فاسدہ میں سے ایک وہ ہے جو بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ عام اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عام اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوتا ہے، جب کہ وہ عام اپنی ذات سے مستقل نہ ہو جیسے اس کا قول نعم او بلى ، یا عام جزاء کی جگہ پر ہو جیسے راوی کا قول سها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسجد كم آنحضرت ملا لیا کہ ہم سے سہو ہوا پس آپ سی نا کہ تم نے سجدہ کیا ، یاوہ عام جواب کے قائم مقام ہو جیسے وہ شخص جس کو ناشتہ کی طرف بلایا گیا ہو اور وہ کہے واللہ میں ناشتہ نہیں کروں گا ، پس بہر حال اس نے زیادتی کر دی جواب کی مقدار پر چنانچہ اس نے کہا واللہ میں آج ناشتہ نہیں کروں گا، تو یہ اختلاف کا مقام ہے پس ہمارے نزدیک وہ از سر نو کلام کرنے والا ہوگا زیادتی کولغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے ۔ ریح : چوتھی وجہ فاسد جس کے قائل امام شافعی ، امام مالک، امام مزنی اور ابوبکر دقاق وغیرہ ہیں ، وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عام صیغہ کسی مخصوص شخص کے بارے میں کسی نص میں یا صحابی کے قول میں وارد ہو تو یہ حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ وہ عام اپنے سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا ، اس عام سے کسی دوسرے کے لئے حکم ثابت نہ ہوگا ، وہ سبب چاہے سائل کا سوال ہو یا کوئی واقعہ ہو، جیسے حضور صلی یا اسلام کے سامنے کسی نے کوئی سوال کیا اور آپ سنی شاہی تم نے عام صیغہ سے جواب ويا من فعل كذا فعليه كذا يا فله كذا یا حضور صل الا اسلام کے زمانے میں کوئی واقعہ پیش آیا اور آپنے عام صیغہ سے کوئی بات ارشاد فرمائی ، تو یہ حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ عام اس سائل کے ساتھ یا صاحب واقعہ کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا ،اس عام سے دوسروں پر حکم نہیں لگے گا، دوسروں پر وہ حکم دوسری نص سے یا قیاس سے لگے گا۔ مگر جمہور اس کے خلاف ہیں ، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ عام کا صیغہ جب کسی خاص سبب سے مقید ہوتو وہ عام اپنے عموم پر رہے گا ،سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوگا ، اور صحابہ اور تابعین کے اجماع سے اس کے نظائر موجود ہیں، جیسے آیت ظہار اوس ابن صامت کی بیوی خولہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ، آیت لعان ہلال ابن امیہ کے بارے میں اور آیت قذف حضرت عائشہ کے بارے میں اور آیت سرقہ حضرت صفوان کی چادر کی چوری میں نازل ہوئی ان سب جگہوں پر صحابہ نے عموم لفظ کا اعتبار کیا ہے۔
And among these (invalid reasons) is what some said: that the general is specified by its cause. And according to us (Hanafis), it is only specified by its cause when it is not independent in itself, like his saying 'yes' or 'no', or when it comes in the context of a condition, like the narrator's saying 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot and prostrated', or when it comes in the context of an answer, like the one invited to breakfast who says, 'By Allah, I will not eat breakfast.' But if he adds beyond the extent of the answer and says, 'By Allah, I will not eat breakfast today', then this is a point of disagreement. According to us, he becomes an initiator (of a new statement) to avoid nullifying the addition. Translation: And among these invalid reasons is that which some people said: that the general is specified by its cause. And according to us, the general is specified by its cause when it is not independent in itself, like his saying 'yes' or 'no', or when it comes in the place of a condition, like the narrator's saying 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot and prostrated', or when it comes in the place of an answer, like the person invited to breakfast who says, 'By Allah, I will not eat breakfast.' In any case, he made an addition beyond the amount of the answer, so he said, 'By Allah, I will not eat breakfast today.' This is a point of disagreement. According to us, he becomes one who initiates speech anew to avoid nullifying the addition. The fourth invalid reason, held by Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Muzani, and Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq etc., is that if a general expression occurs in a text or in a saying of a Companion regarding a specific person, these scholars say that the general will be specified by its cause of occurrence; the ruling from this general will not be established for anyone else. The cause may be a question from a questioner or an incident, like when someone asked a question in the presence of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he replied with a general expression: 'Whoever does such and such, then upon him is such and such' or 'for him is such and such', or an incident occurred during the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and he uttered a general expression. Then these scholars say that the general will be specific to that questioner or the person involved in the incident; the ruling will not apply to others from this general. For others, the ruling will be established from another text or by analogy. But the majority (Jumhūr) are opposed to this. They say that when a general expression is tied to a specific cause, it remains on its generality; it is not specified by the cause of occurrence. And there are precedents from the consensus of the Companions and the Successors. For example, the verse of Zihar was revealed about Khawla, the wife of Aus ibn Samit; the verse of Li'an about Hilal ibn Umayyah; the verse of Qadhf about Aisha; and the verse of Sariqa about the theft of Safwan's cloak. In all these places, the Companions considered the generality of the wording.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul dispute regarding the scope of general statements (al-amm). The Hanafi position (indana) is that a general statement is only specified by its sabab (cause/reason) in three cases: (1) when the general expression is not independent in itself, like 'na'am' (yes) or 'bala' (indeed); (2) when it appears in the context of a conditional sentence (jazā'); and (3) when it appears as a response to a question. If the speaker adds extra words beyond the minimal response, it becomes an independent statement (mubtadi'). The opposing view, attributed to Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and others, holds that if a general expression is uttered regarding a specific person or incident, it is confined to that context. The Jumhūr (majority), which includes the Hanafi school, rejects this and argues that generality remains intact unless there is explicit specification. They cite examples from the Quran where verses were revealed about specific individuals (e.g., Zihar about Khawla, Li'an about Hilal, Qadhf about Aisha, Sariqa about Safwan) yet the Companions applied them generally.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A general expression that encompasses all individuals or items to which it applies.
سبب الورود (sabab al-wurud): The specific cause or occasion that prompted the revelation or utterance of a text.
جمہور (jumhur): The majority of scholars, including the Hanafi school, who hold that 'amm remains general despite its specific cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) In all cases where the cause is known.
B) Only when the general expression is independent in itself.
C) Only when it is non-independent (like yes/no) or appears as a conditional response.
D) Only when the cause is a question from a specific person.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a general statement remains general despite its specific occasion of revelation; explicit specification (takhsis) is required to limit its scope.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
15 min
Restriction of General by Its Specific Occasion
Explains the rule that general is not specified by its cause except in three agreed-upon cases and a disputed fourth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the three agreed-upon exceptions where a general is restricted by its cause from the disputed fourth case, and apply the Hanafi position that the general remains general unless specified by evidence.

Core Idea
A general is not restricted by its cause unless it is dependent, conditional, or an answer.

This passage from Al-Fayd al-Hijazi tackles a critical usul question: does the specific occasion that prompted a general statement narrow its scope? The Hanafi school, supported by the practice of the Companions, insists that the general remains general. However, there are three categories where even Hanafis agree the general is restricted. A fourth case—where the answer adds an extra element—triggers disagreement with other schools. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly deriving rulings from primary texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed rule
Recognize that some scholars (Shafi'i, Malik, etc.) argue that a general expression revealed for a specific incident is restricted to that incident. The Hanafi majority opposes this.
The rule is about 'عام' (general) and 'سبب الورود' (specific cause of revelation).
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi proof is that the Companions applied verses of zihar, li'an, qadhf, and theft generally, even though each was revealed for a specific person or event.
This shows that the cause does not restrict the generality.
3
Learn the three agreed-upon exceptions
Even Hanafis agree that the general is restricted by its cause when: (1) the general is not independent (e.g., 'yes' or 'indeed'), (2) it is a conditional clause (e.g., 'he prostrated' after mention of forgetfulness), (3) it is a direct answer to a statement (e.g., oath regarding a specific invitation).
In these cases, the context necessarily narrows the meaning.
4
Analyze the disputed fourth case
If the answer adds an extra element (like 'today') beyond what is necessary, the Hanafi view is that it becomes an independent statement, preserving the addition's meaning. The other school still treats it as an answer and restricts it.
The key is whether the addition renders the statement independent.
5
Apply the rule to a new example
Given a verse revealed for a specific Companion, does it apply to all Muslims? According to Hanafis, yes, unless there is other evidence of specification. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
۸۵
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
يَكُنْ مُسْتَقِلاً بِنَفْسِهِ كَقَوْلِهِ نَعَمْ أَوْبَلَى اَوْ خَرَجَ مُخْرَجَ الْجَزَاءِ كَقَوْلِ الرَّاوِى سَهَارَسُوْلُ اللهِ صَلَّى الله عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَسَجَدَ أَوْخَرَجَ مُخْرَجَ الْجَوَابَ كَالْمُدْعُو إِلَى الْغَدَاءِ وَيَقُولُ وَاللَّهِ لَا اَتَغَدَى فَأَمَا إِذَازَادَ عَلَى قَدْرِ الْجَوَابِ فَقَالَ وَاللهِ لَا اَتَغَدَى الْيَوْمَ وَهُوَ مَوْضِعُ الْخِلَافِ فَعِنْدَنَا يَصِيْرُ مُبْتَدِأُ احْتَرَارًا عَنْ
أَلْغَاءِ الزِّيَادَةِ ترجمہ: اور ان وجوہ فاسدہ میں سے ایک وہ ہے جو بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ عام اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عام اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوتا ہے، جب کہ وہ عام اپنی ذات سے مستقل نہ ہو جیسے اس کا قول نعم بابلی ، یا عام جزاء کی جگہ پر ہو جیسے راوی کا قول سہا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسجد كم آنحضرت ملا لیا کہ ہم سے سہو ہوا پس آپ سی نا کہ تم نے سجدہ کیا ، یاوہ عام جواب کے قائم مقام ہو جیسے وہ شخص جس کو ناشتہ کی طرف بلایا گیا ہو اور وہ کہے واللہ میں ناشتہ نہیں کروں گا ، پس بہر حال اس نے زیادتی کر دی جواب کی مقدار پر چنانچہ اس نے کہا واللہ میں آج ناشتہ نہیں کروں گا، تو یہ اختلاف کا مقام ہے پس ہمارے نزدیک وہ از سر نو کلام کرنے والا ہوگا زیادتی کولغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے ۔
ریح : چوتھی وجہ فاسد جس کے قائل امام شافعی ، امام مالک، امام مزنی اور ابوبکر دقاق وغیرہ ہیں ، وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر عام صیغہ کسی مخصوص شخص کے بارے میں کسی نص میں یا صحابی کے قول میں وارد ہو تو یہ حضرات کہتے ہیں کہ وہ عام اپنے سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا ، اس عام سے کسی دوسرے کے لئے حکم ثابت نہ ہوگا ، وہ سبب چاہے سائل کا سوال ہو یا کوئی واقعہ ہو، جیسے حضور صلی یا اسلام کے سامنے کسی نے کوئی سوال کیا اور آپ سنی شاہی تم نے عام صیغہ سے جواب ويا من فعل كذا فعليه كذا يا فله كذا یا حضور صل الا اسلام کے زمانے میں کوئی واقعہ پیش آیا اور آپنے عام صیغہ سے کوئی بات ارشاد فرمائی ، تو یہ حضرات فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ عام اس سائل کے ساتھ یا صاحب واقعہ کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا ،اس عام سے دوسروں پر حکم نہیں لگے گا، دوسروں پر وہ حکم دوسری نص سے یا قیاس سے لگے گا۔ مگر جمہور اس کے خلاف ہیں ، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ عام کا صیغہ جب کسی خاص سبب سے مقید ہوتو وہ عام اپنے عموم پر رہے گا ،سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوگا ، اور صحابہ اور تابعین کے اجماع سے اس کے نظائر موجود ہیں، جیسے آیت ظہار اوس ابن صامت کی بیوی خولہ کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ، آیت لعان ہلال ابن امیہ کے بارے میں اور آیت قذف حضرت عائشہ کے بارے میں اور آیت سرقہ حضرت صفوان کی چادر کی چوری میں نازل ہوئی ان سب جگہوں پر صحابہ نے عموم لفظ کا اعتبار کیا ہے
الفيضُ الحجازي
۸۶
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
، ان کو سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص نہیں کیا ہے۔ معلوم ہوا کہ عام لفظ سبب ورود کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوتا ہے بلکہ اپنے عموم پر باقی رہتا ہے۔ البتہ مصنف عاللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تین جگہ ایسی ہیں جہاں عام لفظ کو اس کے سبب کے ساتھ خاص کر دیا جاتا ہے، اپنے عموم پر باقی نہیں رکھا جاتا ہے۔ (۱) پہلی قسم یہ ہے کہ عام مستقل بالذات نہ ہو یعنی ماقبل والے کلام کے بغیر یہ مفید معنی نہ ہو جیسے کسی نے کہا اکان لی علیک الف درهم مخاطب نے جواب میں کہا نعم ، یا کسی نے کہا الیس لی علیک الف درهم مخاطب نے جواب میں کہا ہلی ، تو نعم اور ملی یہ دونوں لفظ عام ہیں، کلام کی بہت سی انواع کا جواب بن سکتے ہیں ،مگر مستقل بنفسہ نہیں ہیں، ماقبل سے متعلق کیے بغیر مفید معنی نہیں ہیں، لہذا یہ سبب کے ساتھ یعنی ماقبل والے کلام کے ساتھ خاص ہو نگے ۔ (۲) دوسری قسم یہ ہے کہ عام جزاء بن رہا ہو تو بھی سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا، کیونکہ جزاء اپنے ماقبل سے مربوط ہوتی ہے جیسے راوی کا قول سها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فسجد تو فسجد پر فا داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے جزاء کے درجہ میں ہے، سجد عام ہے سجدہ سھو ،سجدہ تلاوت، سجدہ نماز سب کا احتمال رکھتا ہے مگر جزاء ہونے کی وجہ سے سبب کے ساتھ یعنی ماقبل والے کلام کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور یہاں سجدہ سہو مراد ہے۔ (۳) تیسری قسم یہ کہ عام جواب کی جگہ پر آرہا ہو ، اگر چہ وہ مستقل کلام ہو، مگر چونکہ جواب ہے لہذا یہ اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہو گا جیسے کسی نے خالد کو کہا آؤ ناشتہ کر لو، خالد نے اس کے جواب میں کہا، اگر میں ناشتہ کروں تو میری بیوی کو تین طلاق ،تو یہ کلام عام ہے جو اس ناشتہ کو بھی شامل ہے ، گھر جا کر ناشتہ کرنے کو بھی شامل ہے ،مگر چونکہ وہ جواب کی جگہ ہے لہذا اسی ناشتہ کے ساتھ یہ کلام خاص ہوگا، اگر گھر جا کر ناشتہ کرے گا تو طلاق نہ پڑے گی۔ ان تین قسموں میں تو عام بالاتفاق اپنے سبب کے ساتھ خاص ہوگا۔ (۴) البتہ ایک چوتھی قسم ہے جس میں اختلاف ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ تیسری قسم میں جو جواب ہے اگر مخاطب اس جواب کی مقدار کو بڑھا کر کہے جیسے اس نے بلایا کہ آؤ ناشتہ کر لو تو خالد نے کہا اگر میں آج ناشتہ کروں تو میری بیوی کو تین طلاق توالیوم کا اضافہ کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ جواب پر محمول نہ ہوگا بلکہ از سر نو کلام یعنی نیا کلام سمجھا جائے گا ، لہذا آج کے دن میں اگر یہ کہیں بھی ناشتہ کرے گا بیوی پر طلاق پڑ جائے گی، یہ عام ہوگا کیونکہ اگر اس کلام کو ماقبل کا جواب قرار دیں تو الیوم کی زیادتی لغو ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ الیوم کے بغیر بھی جواب مکمل ہے، لہذا زیا دتی کولغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے اس کو مستقل کلام مانا جائے گا اور جب مستقل ہو گیا تو اپنے عموم پر رہے گا۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی یہ کلام ماقبل کا جواب ہی سمجھا جائے گا ، اور دلالت حال اس کی دلیل
The general becomes restricted by its cause in three ways: (1) when the general is not independent by itself, like saying 'yes' or 'indeed' in response; (2) when the general comes in the position of a condition (jaza'), like the narrator's statement 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forgot and prostrated'; (3) when the general comes in the position of an answer, like someone invited to lunch saying 'By Allah, I will not eat'. If one adds beyond the measure of the answer, saying 'By Allah, I will not eat today', this is a point of disagreement. According to us (Hanafis), he becomes a new speaker to avoid rendering the addition meaningless. The fourth invalid cause (which Shafi'i, Malik, Muzani, Abu Bakr al-Daqqaq etc. hold) is that if a general expression is revealed concerning a specific person or incident, it becomes restricted to that cause. The majority oppose this, holding that the general remains general, as exemplified by verses of zihar, li'an, qadhf, and theft which were revealed for specific individuals but applied generally by the Companions. The author states that there are three places where the general is restricted by its cause: (1) when it is not independent in meaning, like 'yes' or 'indeed'; (2) when it is a conditional clause, like 'he prostrated' after mention of forgetfulness; (3) when it is an answer to a statement, like the divorce threat regarding lunch. In these three, there is agreement. (4) The fourth type is disputed: if the answer adds a temporal restriction like 'today', we (Hanafis) consider it an independent statement to preserve the addition, while the other school still considers it an answer.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul rule concerning whether a general (عام) statement is restricted (خاص) by its specific occasion (سبب). The author begins by presenting a fourth invalid (فاسد) reason given by some scholars (Shafi'i, Malik, etc.) that general expressions are restricted to their specific causes of revelation or incident. The Hanafi position, supported by the majority (جمہور), is that general expressions remain general and are not restricted by their cause. Evidence is drawn from Quranic verses that were revealed for specific individuals (e.g., verse of zihar for Khawla bint Tha'laba, li'an for Hilal ibn Umayya, qadhf for Aisha, theft for Safwan's cloak) but were applied generally by the Companions. The author then notes that there are three exceptional cases agreed upon where the general is restricted by its cause: (1) when the general is not independent (مستقل بالذات) but depends on prior speech, like 'yes' or 'indeed'; (2) when it functions as a conditional clause (جزاء) linked to a prior condition; (3) when it is an answer (جواب) to a specific statement, like an oath concerning a particular invitation. These are restricted by consensus. The fourth case is a point of ikhtilaf: if the answer adds an extra qualification (like 'today'), the Hanafi ruling is that it becomes an independent statement (مبتدأ) to avoid rendering the addition superfluous, thus the general remains general. The opposing school (Shafi'i etc.) still treats it as an answer and restricts it.

Key Terms
عام ('Aam): A general term that covers all individuals or types without restriction.
سبب (Sabab): The specific cause or occasion that prompted the utterance.
خاص (Khaas): A specific or restricted meaning applied to the general due to evidence or context.
مستقل بالذات (Mustaqill bi al-dhat): Independent in meaning; capable of conveying a complete message without prior context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person is invited to lunch and says 'By Allah, I will not eat lunch today' (adding 'today'), what is the ruling?
A) The statement is restricted to that specific lunch invitation because it is an answer.
B) The statement is general and applies to any lunch that day because the addition makes it an independent statement.
C) The statement is nullified because it is a response to an invitation.
D) The statement only applies if he eats at the inviter's house.

Key Takeaway
A general expression is not restricted by its specific occasion; it remains universal unless explicit evidence of specification exists.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
8 min
The General Word and Its Cause: Consensus Exceptions and Hanafi Position
Rule: General word not specific by cause, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a general word is not restricted by its cause, and distinguish the three consensus exceptions from the fourth disputed case.

Core Idea
A general word remains general unless it is dependent, a result, or an answer—an added word makes it independent.

In this passage, we explore a foundational usul al-fiqh principle: the generality (ʿumūm) of a general word is not confined to the specific occasion that prompted its utterance. However, the scholars identified three instances where the general word must be tied to its cause by consensus, and a fourth case where the Hanafis and others differ. Understanding these nuances is essential for correctly interpreting revealed texts and legal speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default rule
State the principle that a general word remains applicable to all its individuals regardless of the specific cause or context of its utterance.
This is the general principle in Hanafi usul.
2
Recognize exception 1: Dependent words
When the general word cannot stand alone (e.g., 'naʿam' or 'balā'), it is necessarily tied to the preceding statement and thus specific.
These words inherently point back to the cause.
3
Recognize exception 2: Result (jazā')
When a general word appears as the result of a conditional sentence, it is restricted to the condition that triggered it.
Example: 'fasajada' refers specifically to the prostration of forgetfulness, not any prostration.
4
Recognize exception 3: Answer (jawāb)
A general word uttered as an answer to a specific question or invitation is confined to that context.
Example: the 'breakfast' scenario.
5
Analyze the fourth case: Addition of qualifier
If the answer includes an additional word (like 'today'), the Hanafi view treats it as an independent statement, preserving generality. The opposing view relies on contextual indication.
This dispute illustrates the Hanafi preference for explicit wording over inferred context.

ہوگا کیونکہ اگر اس کلام کو ماقبل کا جواب قرار دیں تو الیوم کی زیادتی لغو ہو جائے گی اس لئے کہ الیوم کے بغیر بھی جواب مکمل ہے، لہذا زیا دتی کولغو ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے اس کو مستقل کلام مانا جائے گا اور جب مستقل ہو گیا تو اپنے عموم پر رہے گا۔ ان حضرات کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی یہ کلام ماقبل کا جواب ہی سمجھا جائے گا ، اور دلالت حال اس کی دلیل ہے، یعنی اگر چہ اس نے الیوم کا اضافہ کیا ہے مگر اس کی حالت بتا رہی ہے کہ یہ اسی کھانے کو مراد لے رہا ہے ، اور ہم دلالت حال کا اعتبار اس لئے نہیں کرینگے کہ صریح لفظ آ گیا اس کی رعایت میں اس کو مستقل کلام قرار دینگے۔
They are not made specific by the cause of revelation. It became known that a general word is not specified by its cause of revelation but remains upon its generality. However, the author (may Allah elevate him) says that there are three places where a general word is made specific by its cause, not left upon its generality. (1) The first type is that the general is not independent in essence, i.e., without the preceding speech it does not convey meaning, like if someone said 'Is there owed to me a thousand dirhams upon you?' and the addressee replied 'Na'am' (yes), or if someone said 'Is there not owed to me a thousand dirhams upon you?' and the addressee replied 'Bali' (yes), then these words 'Na'am' and 'Bali' are general, they can be answers to many types of speech, but they are not independent, they do not convey meaning without being connected to what precedes, so they are made specific by the cause, i.e., the preceding speech. (2) The second type is that when the general appears as a result (jaza'), then it is also made specific by the cause, because the result is connected to what precedes it, like the narrator's statement: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) forgot and prostrated', so 'fasajada' with the inclusion of 'fa' is in the position of a result; 'sajada' is general, it can mean prostration of forgetfulness, prostration of recitation, or prostration of prayer, but because it is a result it is specific by the cause, i.e., the preceding speech, and here prostration of forgetfulness is intended. (3) The third type is that the general occurs as an answer, even if it is independent speech, but because it is an answer, it is specific by its cause, like if someone said to Khalid 'Come, have breakfast', Khalid replied 'If I eat breakfast, then my wife is thrice divorced.' This speech is general, it includes this breakfast as well as having breakfast at home. But because it is in the place of answer, it is specific to this breakfast; if he eats breakfast at home, divorce will not occur. In these three types, the general, by consensus, is made specific by its cause. (4) However, there is a fourth type concerning which there is disagreement. It is that in the third type, if the addressee increases the measure of the answer, e.g., if he called 'Come, eat breakfast' and Khalid said 'If I eat breakfast today, then my wife is thrice divorced'—adding 'al-yawm'—then according to us, this will not be considered an answer but will be considered a new speech from the beginning. So if he eats breakfast anywhere today, divorce will occur on his wife. It will be general because if we consider this speech the answer to what preceded, the addition of 'al-yawm' would become superfluous, since the answer is complete without it. Therefore, to avoid the addition being superfluous, it is considered an independent speech, and when it becomes independent, it remains upon its generality. According to those scholars, even in this case this speech is still understood as an answer to what preceded, and the contextual indication (dalalat al-hal) is its proof, meaning that even though he added 'al-yawm', his state indicates that he intends that same meal. And we do not consider the contextual indication because the explicit word came, and by observing it we consider it an independent speech.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage explains a key usul principle: a general word (ʿāmm) is not confined to its specific cause of revelation or context (sabab al-wurūd); it retains its general applicability. However, the author (the commentator) notes three exceptions where the general word is restricted to its cause by consensus, and a fourth case of disagreement. The three exceptions are: (1) when the general word is not independent (e.g., 'naʿam' or 'balā' which need a prior statement), (2) when it functions as the result (jazā') of a conditional clause, (3) when it serves as an answer (jawāb). In these cases, the general word is tied to the specific preceding context. The fourth disputed case is when the answer includes an additional qualifier, like 'today' (al-yawm). The Hanafi position (stated as 'our view') holds that such an addition makes the speech independent, so the general word remains general. The opposing view, relying on contextual indication (dalālat al-ḥāl), still treats it as an answer. The Hanafi argument is that giving weight to the explicit addition (al-yawm) prevents it from being superfluous, thus the speech becomes independent. This illustrates the Hanafi preference for explicit wording over inferred context when both are present.

Key Terms
عام (ʿāmm): A word that, in its linguistic usage, covers all individuals of its category without restriction.
سبب (sabab): The specific occasion or context that gave rise to a ruling or statement.
جزاء (jazāʾ): The result clause in a conditional sentence, which is linked to the condition.
جواب (jawāb): An answer given in response to a question or statement, tied to that context.
دلالة حال (dalālat al-ḥāl): Contextual indication derived from the circumstances surrounding the speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fourth disputed case, why does the Hanafi school consider an answer with an added word like 'اليوم' as independent speech rather than an answer?
A) Because the speaker explicitly stated the word 'اليوم', making it a separate statement.
B) Because the absence of any addition would make the speech ambiguous.
C) Because contextual indication always overrides explicit wording.
D) Because the word 'اليوم' makes the speech incomplete without the preceding clause.

Key Takeaway
A general word remains general unless it is dependent, functions as a result of a conditional, or is an answer; an added word makes the speech independent, preserving generality according to Hanafis.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate

Does the Imperative Imply Repetition?
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i and Ash'ari views on amr and repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether the imperative (amr) implies repetition, explain the linguistic proof, and contrast it with the Shafi'i and Ash'ari positions.

Core Idea
The imperative demands a single performance of the act, not repetition—because the underlying masdar is a single instance that cannot accommodate number.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul dispute: does a command (like 'pray!') require repeated performance or just one? The Hanafi answer is rooted in the linguistic structure of the command form. You will explore the three schools' views and see how the example of divorce (talaq) illustrates the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Note the Hanafi position (no repetition, no bearing), the Shafi'i position (no necessitation but bears repetition), and the Ash'ari (Abu Ishaq) position (necessitates repetition). Distinguish between 'mujib' and 'muhtamil'.
2
Analyse the Hanafi linguistic proof
Understand that the imperative form is abbreviated from 'demand of an action' and the action (masdar) is a single instance (fard) that cannot accept number.
3
Examine the Shafi'i counter-argument
The Shafi'i holds that the masdar in the original phrase is indefinite (nakira), which can imply generality and thus bear repetition.
4
Examine the Ash'ari counter-argument
Abu Ishaq uses the hadith of Hajj where a Companion asked 'is it for this year or forever?' to argue that the imperative necessitates repetition.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the dispute to the example of a husband saying 'talliqi nafsak' to his wife. Hanafi: only one divorce is effected (unless the wife is a slave-girl). Shafi'i: the command allows potential for more, but does not require. Ash'ari: would require repetition unless evidence shows otherwise.

Source Text

وَلَا مُوجَبَ لَهُ فِي التَّكْرَارِ وَلَا يَحْتَمِلُهُ لاَنَ لَفْظَ الْأَمْرِ صِيْغَةٌ أُخْتُصِرَتْ لِمَعْنَاهَا مِنْ طَلَب الْفِعْلِ لكِنَّ لَفْظَ الْفِعْلِ فَرْدْ فَلَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْعَدَدَ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا فِي قَوْلِ الرَّجُلِ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ طَلَقِىٰ نَفْسَكِ إِنَّهُ يَقَعُ عَلَى الْوَاحِدَةِ وَلَا تُعْمَلُ نِيَةُ الثَّنْتَيْنِ فِيْهِ لأَنَّهُ لا تَصِعُ نِيَةُ الْعَدَدِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ الْمَرْأَةُ آمَةً لِاَنَ ذَلِكَ جِئْسُ طَلَاقِهَا فَصَارَ مِنْ طَرِيقِ الْجِنْسِ وَاحِدًا ترجمہ : ۔ اور نہیں ہے امر کا موجب تکرار میں اور نہ تکرار کا احتمال رکھتا ہے، اس لئے کہ لفظ امر ایک صیغہ ہے جس کو اس کے معنی کے لئے طلب فعل سے مختصر کیا گیا ہے لیکن لفظ فعل ( مصدر ) فرد ہے تو وہ عدد کا احتمال نہیں رکھے گا، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا مرد کے قول میں اپنی بیوی سے طلقی نفسک کہ تو اپنے آپ کو طلاق دیدے تو یہ قول واقع ہوگا ایک طلاق پر اور اس میں نہیں عمل کیا جائے گا دو کی نیت پر، اس لئے کہ یہ عدد کی نیت ہے مگر یہ کہ عورت باندی ہو، اس لئے کہ یہ دو اس کی طلاق کی جنس ہے پس یہ دو جنس کے طریقہ سے ایک ہو جائے گی۔
شریح:- مصنف عاللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امر وجوب کے اعتبار سے تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا ہے، لہذا جب صل کہا تو ایک مرتبہ نماز پڑھنا واجب ہوگا ، یہی احناف کا مذہب ہے، اشاعرہ میں سے ابو احق اسفرائنی کہتے ہیں کہ امر کا موجب تکرار ہے یعنی امر تکرار کا تقاضا کرتا ہے، اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ امر کا موجب تکرار نہیں ہے یعنی امر تکرار کا تقاضا تو نہیں کرتا ہے، البتہ امرتکرار کا مکمل ہے یعنی امر میں تکرار کا احتمال ہوتا ہے، موجب اور مشتمل میں فرق یہ ہے کہ موجب بغیر نیت کے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور محتمل بغیر نیت کے ثابت نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور
امام شافعی اللہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ امر کا صیغہ اضرب مختصر کیا گیا ہے، اصل عبارت ہے اَطْلُبُ مِنْكَ ضَرْباً اس کو مختصر کر کے اضرب کہا، اور اطلب منک ضر بائیں ضرب مصدر نکرہ ہے، پس اس کا مختصر جو اضرب ہے وہ بھی ضرب نکرہ کو شامل ہے اور نکرہ اگر چہ خاص ہوتا ہے مگر عموم کا احتمال رکھتا ہے لہذا امر میں تکرار کا احتمال رہے گا۔ ابو الحق اسفرائینی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب حج کی فرضیت ہوئی تو حضور صلی با اسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا إِنَّ اللَّهَ كَتَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الْحَجُّ تو اقرع بن حابس رضی اللہ عنہ نے فرمایا أَلِعَامِنَا هَذَا يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ لَمْ لِلْأَبَدِ کیا اسی سال یا ہر سال فرض ہے ، اقرع بن حابس نے امر سے تکرار کو سمجھا ، جب کہ وہ صاحب زبان ہے، ورنہ یہ سوال نہ کرتے ، معلوم ہوا کہ امر کا موجب تکرا ر ہے۔
احناف کی دلیل مصنف یہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ لفظ امر فعل کو مصدر سے طلب کرنے سے مختصر کیا گیا ہے یعنی اضْرب ، أطلب مِنْكَ الضَّرْب سے مختصر کیا گیا ہے، تو امر میں مصدر ملحوظ ہے اور مصدر جس کو مصنف نے لفظ الفعل سے تعبیر کیا ہے فرد ہے اور فرد عدد کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا ہے، کیونکہ فرد اور عدد میں منافات ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ امر میں نہ تکرار ہوتی ہے اور نہ تکرار کا احتمال ہوتا ہے۔ ولهذا قلنا: -مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ امر میں تکرار اور عدد کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا ہے، اس لئے اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا طلقی نفسک تو اپنے آپ پر طلاق واقع کر ، اور کوئی نیت نہیں کی تو عورت صرف ایک طلاق واقع کرسکتی ہے اور اگر شوہر نے تین طلاقوں کی نیت کی تو اس کو تین طلاق واقع کرنے کا حق ہوگا لیکن اگر شوہر دو کی نیت کرتا ہے تو اس کی نیت معتبر نہ ہوگی اور عورت کو دو طلاق واقع کرنے کا حق نہ ہوگا، اس لئے کہ طلقی مختصر کیا گیا ہے اور وہ مصدر تطلیق پر مشتمل ہے اور مصدر فرد ہوتا ہے، اس میں عدد کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا ہے ،لہذا ایک ہی طلاق وہ واقع کر سکتی ہے، کیونکہ ایک فرد حقیقی ہے، اور اگر شوہر نے تین کی نیت کی ہے تو وہ تین بھی واقع کر سکتی ہے کیونکہ تین پوری جنس کا مجموعہ ہے، اور مجموعہ حکما فر ہی کہا جاتا ہے، لہذا تین فرد حکمی ہے عرض فرد کی دو قسمیں ہیں فرد حقیقی جیسے حقیقت ایک اور فرد حکمی یعنی پوری جنس کا مجموعہ، یہ بھی حکما فرد ہی ہے۔ تو امر میں فرد حقیقی تو اس کا موجب ہوتا ہے جو بغیر نیت کے ثابت ہوجاتا ہے اور فرد کمی امر کا حمل ہوتا ہے جو نیت سے ثابت ہو جائے گا، البتہ دو طلاق مراد نہیں ہوسکتی ہے،اس لئے کہ دو عدد ہے نہ فرد حقیقی ہے نہ حکمی ، ہاں اگر باندی سے کہا تو دو کی بھی نیت کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ باندی کے حق میں دو طلاقیں پوری جنس طلاق ہے یعنی فرد کی ہے۔
And the imperative does not necessitate repetition nor does it bear it, because the word of command is a form abbreviated for its meaning from the demand of an action, but the word of the action (the masdar) is a single instance, so it does not bear number. For this reason we said concerning a man's statement to his wife 'talliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) that it falls as one divorce, and the intention of two is not effective in it, because the intention of number is not valid unless the woman is a slave-girl, because that (two) is the type (jins) of her divorce, so it becomes one by way of the type. Translation: And the imperative does not necessitate repetition nor does it bear repetition, because the word of command is a form that has been abbreviated for its meaning from the demand of an action, but the word of the action (the masdar) is a single instance, so it will not bear number. And for this reason we said concerning a man's statement to his wife 'talliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself) that this statement will occur as one divorce, and the intention of two will not be acted upon, because it is an intention of number, unless the woman is a slave-girl, because two is the type of her divorce, so these two become one by way of the type. Commentary: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says that the imperative, in terms of obligation, does not require repetition; thus when He said 'pray', praying once becomes obligatory. This is the Hanafi school. Among the Ash'arites, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini says that the imperative necessitates repetition, i.e., the imperative requires repetition. Imam al-Shafi'i says that the imperative does not necessitate repetition, i.e., the imperative does not require repetition, but it is capable of repetition, meaning the imperative has the potential for repetition. The difference between 'necessitating' (mujib) and 'bearing' (muhtamil) is that the necessitating is established without intention, while the bearing is not established without intention. And Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that the imperative form 'idrib' is abbreviated, the original phrase is 'atlabu minka darban' (I demand from you a striking). This was abbreviated to 'idrib'. And 'atlabu minka darban' – 'darb' is an indefinite masdar, so its abbreviated form 'idrib' also includes the indefinite 'darb'. And an indefinite noun, although specific, carries the potential for generality, so the imperative bears the potential for repetition. Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini's proof is that when Hajj was made obligatory, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said 'Indeed Allah has prescribed Hajj upon you'. Then Aqra' ibn Habis (may Allah be pleased with him) said 'Is it for this year, O Messenger of Allah, or forever?' Aqra' ibn Habis understood repetition from the command, and he is a master of the language. Otherwise he would not have asked. So it is known that the imperative necessitates repetition. The Hanafi proof, which the author is explaining, is that the word of command is abbreviated from demanding the action from the masdar, i.e., 'idrib' is abbreviated from 'atlabu minka ad-darb'. So the imperative has the masdar in view, and the masdar, which the author called 'the word of the action', is a single instance (fard), and a single instance does not bear number, because there is a conflict between a single instance and number. So it is known that the imperative has neither repetition nor the potential for repetition. For this reason we said: The author says that the imperative does not bear repetition or number. Therefore, if someone says to his wife 'talliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself), and he has no intention, the woman can only effect one divorce. And if the husband intends three divorces, he has the right to effect three divorces. But if the husband intends two, his intention is not considered, and the woman does not have the right to effect two divorces, because 'talliqi' is abbreviated and it comprises the masdar of tatliq, and the masdar is a single instance, it does not bear number. So she can only effect one divorce, because one is a true single instance (fard haqiqi). And if the husband intends three, she can effect three because three is the sum of the entire type (jins), and the sum is considered a single instance (fard) legally. Thus three is a legal single instance (fard hukmi). There are two types of single instance: true single instance like the reality of one, and legal single instance which is the sum of the entire type; this too is legally a single instance. So in the command, the true single instance is what it necessitates and is established without intention, and the legal single instance is what the command carries and is established with intention. However, two divorces cannot be intended because two is a number, neither a true single instance nor a legal one. Yes, if he says to a slave-girl, he can also intend two, because for a slave-girl, two divorces are the entire type of divorce, i.e., it is a single instance.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a madhhab dispute (usul dispute) concerning whether the imperative (amr) implies repetition or not. The author (مصنف) states the Hanafi position: the imperative does not necessitate repetition nor does it even bear the possibility of repetition. The reason is linguistic: the imperative form is an abbreviation of 'I demand an action from you', and the action (masdar) is a single entity (fard), which cannot accommodate number. To illustrate, the author gives the example of a husband telling his wife 'talliqi nafsak' (divorce yourself). According to the Hanafi view, this command results in only one divorce unless the wife is a slave-girl (where two divorces constitute the entire type of divorce for her). The passage then presents three positions: the Hanafi (no repetition, no bearing), that of Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini (repetition is necessitated), and that of Imam al-Shafi'i (repetition is not necessitated but is possible). The key distinction is between 'mujib' (necessitating) and 'muhtamil' (bearing/potential). For the Shafi'i position, the imperative can bear repetition because the masdar is indefinite (nakira), which can imply generality. For Abu Ishaq, the prophetic hadith where Aqra' ibn Habis asked about Hajj shows that repetition was understood. The Hanafi rebuttal reaffirms that the masdar is a single instance, so the command only covers one performance. The passage elaborates with the distinction between fard haqiqi (true single instance, like one divorce) and fard hukmi (legal single instance, like three divorces which collectively are treated as a single type for a free woman). Thus, in commands, intention can affect whether the command is fulfilled by a single or multiple instances, but the command itself does not require repetition.

Key Terms
امر (amr): A command; a linguistic form used to demand an action.
تکرار (takrar): Repetition; performing the commanded act more than once.
موجب (mujib): That which necessitates something; the imperative as a cause that requires the commanded act to be performed (once or repetitively).
محتمل (muhtamil): That which bears or allows for something; the imperative that can be interpreted to include repetition but does not require it.
فرد (fard): A single instance or unit; that which is one and cannot be divided into smaller units in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view on the imperative (amr), which of the following best describes the ruling when a husband says to his free wife 'talliqi nafsak' without any intention?
A) She can only affect one divorce.
B) She can affect two divorces because the command can bear repetition.
C) She can affect three divorces.
D) The command is invalid because it is a vague command.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the imperative (amr) demands a single performance and does not imply repetition, a position derived from the linguistic nature of the masdar as a single instance (fard).

Part of Time as Cause in Temporal Obligations
Resolving the dual role of time as container and cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that only the part of time adjacent to performance serves as the cause (sabab) for temporal obligations, and distinguish the Hanafi position from Imam Zufar's regarding the extent of causation transfer.

Core Idea
In temporal obligations, the cause is the part of time adjacent to the act, not the whole interval.

The Hanafi school resolves a tension in the concept of muwaqqat bil-waqt (temporal obligations) by specifying that only a part of the time—the part immediately connected to the act—acts as the cause (sabab) for obligation. This preserves both the container (zarf) and cause roles of time. The passage outlines the reasoning, explores four performance scenarios, and addresses a dispute with Imam Zufar over the final portion of time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Recognize the apparent conflict: time as container requires the act within time; as cause requires act after time.
The resolution lies in not making the entire time a cause.
2
State the Hanafi Solution
The cause is the part of time connected to the performance (e.g., the moment before tahrimah).
This minimal part avoids contradiction.
3
Enumerate the Four Scenarios
List the four cases: at the beginning, after beginning, at the last part (tahrimah measure), and after time (qada).
Different parts serve as cause depending on when performance occurs.
4
Analyze the Dispute with Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar requires time for four rak'at; Hanafis accept only the tahrimah part.
The Hanafi response invokes nominal ability (hukm al-qudra) vs actual ability.
5
Apply the Principle to New Cases
Use the rule to determine obligation when only the last moment remains.
The obligation stands even if the full prayer cannot be completed.

پس پورے وقت کو سبب بنانے میں یہ خرابیاں لازم آ رہی ہیں، تو مصنف نے فرماتے ہیں کہ سبب وقت کے بعض حصہ کو بنائیں گے اور وہ وقت کا وہ جزء لا تجری ہے جس کے ساتھ نماز کی ادا متصل ہے یعنی تحریمہ سے پہلے والا پس کہتے ہیں کہ اگر ادا پہلے جزء سے متصل ہوئی تو یہی پہلا جزء سبب ہوگا ، اگر پہلے جزء میں ادا نہ پائی گئی تو سبیت اگلے اجزاء کی طرف منتقل ہوتی رہے گی۔ اس طرح پورے وقت کو چھوڑ کر ایک جزء کو سبب بنانے کی ضرورت اس لئے پیش آئی کہ پورے وقت کو سبب بنانے میں ظرفیت یا سبیت کے معنی فوت ہورہے تھے تو پورے وقت سے سبیت کو منتقل کرنا ضروری ٹھہرا اور پورے وقت کے بعد ایسا کوئی معین حصہ جیسے خمس ، ربع وغیرہ بھی نہیں تھا کہ جس کی طرف ہم سب کو منتقل کرتے ، اور کہتے کہ یہ چوتھائی حصہ یا وقت کا تہائی حصہ سبب ہے، کیوں کہ پورے وقت میں نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے، لہذا جب کوئی معین حصہ بھی نہیں ہے اور پورے وقت کو بھی سبب نہیں بنا سکتے تو ادنی مقدار پر اکتفاء کرنا ضروری ہوا اور ادنی مقدار وہ جزء ہے جس کے ساتھ ادا متصل ہے کیونکہ یہ جز ءادا سے ملا ہوا ہے اور اصل سبب میں یہ ہے کہ وہ مسبب سے ملا ہوا ہو۔ ولم يجز تقديرة :- سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے کہ آپ ادا سے متصل جزء کو سبب قرار دے رہے ہیں، تو صرف ادا سے متصل جزء کو سبب قرار دینے کے بجائے ادا سے پہلے گزرے ہوئے تمام اجزاء کو سبب قرار دیں تو کیا حرج ہے؟
اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ ادا سے پہلے گذرے ہوئے تمام اسباب کو سبب قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے، کیونکہ دلیل کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ پورا وقت سبب ہو جیسے قضا میں ہوتا ہے، یا وہ ادنی جزء سبب ہو کیونکہ یہ ادا سے ملا ہوا ہے، اور اصل سبب میں یہ ہے کہ وہ مسبب سے ملا ہوا ہو ، اور ان دو کے علاوہ کو سبب بنانے کی کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، لہذا ادا اور سے پہلے کے تمام اجزاء کو سبب بنانے میں قلیل ( جزء متصل بالا دا) سے بغیر دلیل کے اعراض و تجاوز لازم آ رہا ہے جو جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہاں اگر کوئی دلیل ہوتی تو گزرے ہوئے اجزا کو سبب بنا سکتے تھے ،مگر کوئی دلیل نہیں ہے، لہذا اقلیل یعنی جزء متصل بالا داء سے تجاوز نہ کریں گے۔
ثم كذلك - مصنف االلہ کہتے ہیں کہ سبیت پہلے جزء سے منتقل ہوتی رہے گی یہاں تک کہ ہمارے نزد یک آخری جزء تک جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جب چار رکعت کے بقدر وقت باقی رہ جائے ، وہاں تک سبیت منتقل ہوگی ، اب اس کے بعد سبیت آگے منتقل نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ اگر چار رکعت کے بقدر وقت باقی نہیں رہا اور آپ نے وقت کو سبب بنا کر چار رکعت واجب کر دی تو یہ بندہ پر تکلیف مالا يطاق ہے ، اور احناف کے نزدیک ادا شروع کرنے سے متصل جو آخری جزء ہے جو تحریمہ کی مقدار ہے وہاں تک سبیت منتقل ہوگی، کیونکہ یہ آخری جزء ہے اس کے بعد کوئی جزء نہیں جس کی طرف سبیت کو منتقل کیا جا سکے۔ سوال: - احناف تحریمہ کی مقدار آخری جزء کو سبب قرار دے رہے ہیں ،جس میں صرف تحریمہ کے بقدر وقت ہے، پوری نماز پڑھ سکے اتنا وقت نہیں ہے، تو کیا اس سے تکلیف مالا يطاق لازم نہیں آئے گی ؟ جواب: - امام ابو حنیفہ عالی کے نزدیک ادا واجب ہونے کے لئے حقیقہ قدرت شرط نہیں ہے، تو ہم قدرت کافی ہے، پس تحریمہ کے بقدر جو آخری جزء ہے اس میں اگر چہ بندہ ادا پر حقیقۂ قدرت نہیں رکھتا ہے کیونکہ وقت ہی
Explanation: A question arises: In the first type of muwaqqat bil-waqt, where time is both a container and a cause for the commanded act, how can these two be combined? Because as a container, it requires the commanded act to be performed within the time, but as a cause, it requires the commanded act to be performed after the time because the cause precedes the effect. The author (صلى الله عليه وسلم) responds: In the first type, when we make time a container and a cause for obligation, we cannot make the entire time a cause. If we make the entire time a cause, then either the meaning of container or the meaning of cause will be lost, or both, because there are three scenarios for performing the commanded act: (1) performed after the time, (2) performed before the time, (3) performed within the time. If the first scenario (performed after the time), the meaning of cause is preserved because cause precedes effect, but the meaning of container is lost because performance is delayed. If the second (performed before the time), both container and cause are lost because it is not within time and cause does not precede effect; rather, the effect precedes the cause. If the third (performed within the time), the meaning of container is preserved but cause is lost because both occur simultaneously. So these defects arise from making the entire time a cause. The author says: We will make a part of time the cause, and that part is the indivisible moment (جزء لا تجری) which is connected to the performance of the prayer, i.e., the moment before the tahrimah. Then there are four scenarios: (1) Prayer performed at the beginning of time: the first part is the cause. (2) If performed after the beginning: the part connected to the performance from the subsequent parts is the cause. (3) If the parts pass and the last (deficient) part arrives: that deficient part becomes the cause, like in Asr prayer. (4) If the entire time passes and one is now performing (qada): the entire time becomes the cause, because the obstacle to making the whole time a cause is removed. These four scenarios the author will mention in the next phrase. Then he says: If performance is connected to the first part, that first part is the cause. If performance is not found in the first part, causation transfers to the subsequent parts. Thus, the necessity of making a single part the cause arose because making the entire time a cause would lose the meanings of container and cause. So it became necessary to transfer causation from the entire time. And after the entire time, there is no specific portion like one-fifth or one-quarter to which we could transfer causation, because one can pray throughout the time. Since there is no specific portion and we cannot make the entire time a cause, it was necessary to be satisfied with the minimal amount, and that minimal amount is the part connected to the performance because it is adjacent to the act, and the essence of causation is that it is connected to the effect. 'And it is not permissible to estimate (a larger part)': This is the answer to an implied question: Since you are making the part connected to performance the cause, why not make all the preceding parts the cause instead of just the connected part? He responds: Making all the preceding parts the cause is not correct because the evidence requires either the entire time to be the cause (as in qada) or the minimal part (the one connected to performance). There is no evidence for anything else. So deviating from the minimal part (the connected part) without evidence would be a transgression, which is not permissible. Yes, if there were evidence, we could make the preceding parts the cause, but there is no evidence. Therefore, we will not exceed the minimal part, i.e., the part connected to performance. Then likewise: The author says that causation transfers from the first part until, according to us (Hanafis), the last part which is the measure of tahrimah, and according to Imam Zufar, until when the remaining time equals the measure of four rak'at. After that, causation does not transfer further because if there is not enough time for four rak'at and you make time a cause to obligate four rak'at, that would be an unbearable burden. According to the Hanafis, causation transfers up to the last part connected to the start of performance, which is the measure of tahrimah, because that is the last part and there is no part after to which causation can transfer. Question: The Hanafis make the last part of the measure of tahrimah the cause, in which there is only time for tahrimah, not enough to pray the entire prayer. Does this not lead to an unbearable burden? Answer: According to Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), actual ability (haqiqat al-qudra) is not a condition for obligation; nominal ability (hukm al-qudra) is sufficient. So in the last part of the measure of tahrimah, even though the servant does not have actual ability to perform, because the time is

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh commentary explaining the rule regarding muwaqqat bil-waqt (temporal obligations). The author addresses a key problem: how can time be both a container (zarf) and a cause (sabab) for an obligation like daily prayers? The apparent conflict is that a container requires the act to happen within it, while a cause requires the act to happen after it (since cause precedes effect). The Hanafi solution is that the entire time cannot be the cause; rather, only the part of time immediately connected to the performance of the act serves as the cause. This preserves both roles: the time as container holds the act within its interval, while the specific part as cause triggers the obligation. The commentary then enumerates four scenarios based on when the act is performed: at the beginning, middle, end (with only enough time for the opening takbir), or after the time (qada). In qada, the entire time becomes the cause because the obstacle of preserving container-meaning no longer applies. The text also addresses an objection: why not take all preceding parts as cause? The answer is that evidence only supports either the entire time (in qada) or the manifestly connected part; anything else is baseless. Finally, there is a dispute with Imam Zufar: he holds that causation transfers up to the point where four rak'at remain, while the Hanafis (Abu Hanifa and his disciples) hold it transfers up to the last part sufficient for the opening takbir (tahrimah). The question of unbearable burden is answered by the Hanafi principle that nominal ability (hukm al-qudra) suffices for obligation, not actual ability (haqiqat al-qudra). This is a sophisticated usul analysis demonstrating how Hanafi usul reconciles apparent contradictions through careful specification of the cause (sabab).

Key Terms
موقت بالوقت (muwaqqat bil-waqt): An obligation that is defined by a specific time interval, like the five daily prayers.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation; in temporal obligations, it is a part of the time.
ظرف (zarf): The container or timeframe within which the act is performed.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer.
تکلیف مالا یطاق (taklif ma la yutaq): An unbearable burden; obligating something impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul as explained in the text, what is the cause (sabab) for the obligation of a temporal act like prayer?
A) The entire time period of the prayer.
B) The part of time immediately connected to the performance of the prayer.
C) The intention (niyyah) to pray.
D) The last part of time equal to four rak'at.

Key Takeaway
In temporal obligations, the cause is the part of time immediately connected to the performance, preserving both the container and cause roles.

Time as Measure: The Second Type of Time-Bound Command
Explaining the second type and its ruling with sick/traveler distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when time is a measure (miyar), any intention during that time defaults to the specified obligation, and distinguish the rulings for the sick and traveler based on the cause of their concession.

Core Idea
When time measures the act, the act fills the time; no other act of its genus can fit.

The author distinguishes between two types of time-bound commands: in the first, time is a container (zarf); in the second, time is a measure (miyar) that defines the act's extent. The Ramadan fast exemplifies this: the day is the measure of the fast, so the fast is co-extensive with the daylight. This lesson unpacks the legal consequences: any intention during that time defaults to the specified obligation, with an important exception for the traveler based on the nature of his concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of time-bound commands
Recall that commands may be time-bound with time as container (zarf) or as measure (miyar). The second type is defined by the act being co-extensive with the time.
Compare with first type where the act could be done anytime within the time period.
2
Apply the rule to a healthy resident in Ramadan
Any intention (absolute, nafl, qada, kaffarah, nadhr) automatically counts as the Ramadan fast; mistaken descriptions are void because the time is specified for that obligation.
This is the default rule for all who are not exempted by a concession.
3
Distinguish the sick and traveler using the cause of concession
The sick have a concession based on actual inability (hqiqi), so fasting proves ability and attaches them to the healthy. The traveler's concession is based on presumed inability (taqdiri) from travel, which remains even if he fasts.
Thus the traveler can, by intending another wajib, fulfill that wajib; the sick cannot.
4
Analyse the rational proof (talil) for the distinction
The cause (illah) for the sick is actual inability; for the traveler, presumed inability. Since the cause differs, the rulings differ. This is a qiyas-based argument within the usul framework.
The author states this is the sahih qawl of the Hanafi school.
